            <li>70.2% <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a></li>
            <li>26.3% Christians</li>
            <li>3.5% others</li>
           </ul>
          </div></td>
        </tr>

      <p><b>Kazakhstan</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[e]</a></sup> officially the <b>Republic of Kazakhstan</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[f]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[13]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">transcontinental country</a> mainly located in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> with a smaller portion west of the <a href="/wiki/Ural_(river)" title="Ural (river)">Ural River</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>. It covers a land area of 2,724,900 square kilometres (1,052,100&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), and shares land borders with <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> in the north, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> in the east, and <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a> in the south while also adjoining a large part of the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> in the southwest. Kazakhstan does not border <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, although they are only 37 kilometers apart. </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan is the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_land_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and outlying territories by land area">eighth-largest country</a> in the world. It has a population of 18.8&nbsp;million residents, and has <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population density">one of the lowest population densities</a> in the world, at fewer than 6 people per square kilometre (15 people per sq mi). Since 1997, the capital is <a href="/wiki/Nur-Sultan" title="Nur-Sultan">Nur-Sultan</a>, formerly known as Astana. It was moved from <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, the country's largest city. </p>
      <p>The territory of Kazakhstan has historically been inhabited by nomadic groups and empires. In antiquity, the nomadic <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a> inhabited the land and the Persian <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a> expanded towards the southern territory of the modern country. <a href="/wiki/Turkic_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkic people">Turkic</a> <a href="/wiki/Nomads" class="mw-redirect" title="Nomads">nomads</a>, who trace their ancestry to many <a href="/wiki/List_of_Turkic_dynasties_and_countries" title="List of Turkic dynasties and countries">Turkic states</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/First_Turkic_Khaganate" title="First Turkic Khaganate">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Turkic_Khaganate" title="Second Turkic Khaganate">Second Turkic Khaganates</a>, have inhabited the country throughout its history. In the 13th century, the territory was subjugated by the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> under <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a>. By the 16th century, the <a href="/wiki/Kazakhs" title="Kazakhs">Kazakh</a> emerged as a distinct group, divided into three <i><a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCz" class="mw-redirect" title="Jüz">jüz</a></i>. The <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> began advancing into the <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_steppe" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazakh steppe">Kazakh steppe</a> in the 18th century, and by the mid-19th century, they nominally ruled all of Kazakhstan as part of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>. Following the 1917 <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a>, and subsequent <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">civil war</a>, the territory of Kazakhstan was reorganised several times. In 1936, it was made the <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic">Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. Kazakhstan was the last of the <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">Soviet republics</a> to declare independence during the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991. The first <a href="/wiki/President_of_Kazakhstan" title="President of Kazakhstan">president of Kazakhstan</a> was characterised as an authoritarian, and <a href="/wiki/Nursultan_Nazarbayev#Presidency" title="Nursultan Nazarbayev">his government</a> was accused of numerous human rights violations, including suppression of dissent and censorship of the media. <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> says that "Kazakhstan heavily restricts freedom of assembly, speech, and religion."<sup id="cite_ref-World_Report_2015:_Kazakhstan_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Report_2015:_Kazakhstan-20">[14]</a></sup> Other human rights organisations regularly describe <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Kazakhstan" title="Human rights in Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan's human rights situation</a> as poor. </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan is the most dominant nation of Central Asia economically, generating 60% of the region's GDP, primarily through its oil and gas industry. It also has vast mineral resources,<sup id="cite_ref-time_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time-21">[15]</a></sup> and is officially a democratic, secular, unitary, constitutional republic with a diverse cultural heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[16]</a></sup> Kazakhstan is a member of the United Nations (UN), <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organization">Shanghai Cooperation Organization</a> (SCO), the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Union" title="Eurasian Economic Union">Eurasian Economic Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective Security Treaty Organisation">CSTO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">OIC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkic_Council" title="Turkic Council">CCTS</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Turkic_Council" title="Turkic Council">Turkic Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_of_Turkic_Culture" title="International Organization of Turkic Culture">TURKSOY</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
      <p>The name "Kazakh" comes from the <a href="/wiki/Old_Turkic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Turkic language">ancient Turkic</a> word <i lang="otk-Latn" title="Old Turkic-language text">qaz</i>, "to wander", reflecting the Kazakhs' <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_nomads" title="Eurasian nomads">nomadic</a> culture.<sup id="cite_ref-etym_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etym-23">[17]</a></sup> The term "<a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossack</a>" is of the same origin.<sup id="cite_ref-etym_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etym-23">[17]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> suffix <i lang="fa-Latn" title="Persian-language text"><a href="/wiki/-stan" title="-stan">-stan</a></i> means "land" or "place of", so <i>Kazakhstan</i> can be literally translated as "land of the wanderers". </p>
      <p>Though the term traditionally referred to only <a href="/wiki/Kazakhs" title="Kazakhs">ethnic Kazakhs</a>, including those living in China, Russia, Turkey, Uzbekistan and other neighbouring countries, the term <i>Kazakh</i> is increasingly being used to refer to any inhabitant of Kazakhstan, including non-Kazakhs.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[18]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Kazakhstan" title="History of Kazakhstan">History of Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cumania_(1200)_eng.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Cumania_%281200%29_eng.png/270px-Cumania_%281200%29_eng.png" decoding="async" width="270" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Cumania_%281200%29_eng.png/405px-Cumania_%281200%29_eng.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Cumania_%281200%29_eng.png/540px-Cumania_%281200%29_eng.png 2x" data-file-width="1141" data-file-height="500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cumania_(1200)_eng.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Cumania" title="Cumania">Cuman–Kipchak confederation</a> in Eurasia circa 1200. The Kazakhs are descendants of <a href="/wiki/Kipchaks" title="Kipchaks">Kipchaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nogai_Horde" title="Nogai Horde">Nogais</a> and other Turkic and medieval Mongol tribes
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kazakhstan has been inhabited since the <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">Paleolithic</a> era.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[19]</a></sup> Pastoralism developed during the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a>, as the region's climate and terrain are best suited for a nomadic lifestyle. </p>
      <p>The Kazakh territory was a key constituent of the Eurasian trading <a href="/wiki/Steppe_Route" title="Steppe Route">Steppe Route</a>, the ancestor of the terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road_UNESCO_World_Heritage_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="Silk Road UNESCO World Heritage Sites">Silk Roads</a>. Archaeologists believe that humans first <a href="/wiki/Domestication_of_the_horse" title="Domestication of the horse">domesticated the horse</a> (i.e., ponies) in the region's vast steppes. During recent prehistoric times, Central Asia was inhabited by groups such as the possibly Proto-Indo-European <a href="/wiki/Afanasievo_culture" title="Afanasievo culture">Afanasievo culture</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[20]</a></sup> later early Indo-Iranians cultures such as <a href="/wiki/Andronovo_culture" title="Andronovo culture">Andronovo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Beckwith49_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beckwith49-27">[21]</a></sup> and later Indo-Iranians such as the <a href="/wiki/Saka" title="Saka">Saka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Massagetae" title="Massagetae">Massagetae</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-B_68_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-B_68-28">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-D_37_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D_37-29">[23]</a></sup> Other groups included the nomadic <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a> and the Persian <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a> in the southern territory of the modern country. In 329 BC, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Macedonians" title="Ancient Macedonians">Macedonian</a> army fought in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jaxartes" title="Battle of Jaxartes">Battle of Jaxartes</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a> along the Jaxartes River, now known as the <a href="/wiki/Syr_Darya" title="Syr Darya">Syr Darya</a> along the southern border of modern Kazakhstan. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kazakh_Khanate">Kazakh Khanate</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Khanate" title="Kazakh Khanate">Kazakh Khanate</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Abylai_Khan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Abylai_Khan.jpg/150px-Abylai_Khan.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Abylai_Khan.jpg/225px-Abylai_Khan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2a/Abylai_Khan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="299" data-file-height="388"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Abylai_Khan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ablai_Khan" title="Ablai Khan">Ablai Khan</a>, khan of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_j%C3%BCz" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle jüz">Middle jüz</a> from 1771 to 1781
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuman_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuman people">Cuman</a> entered the steppes of modern-day Kazakhstan around the early 11th century, where they later joined with the <a href="/wiki/Kipchak_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kipchak people">Kipchak</a> and established the vast Cuman-Kipchak confederation. While ancient cities <a href="/wiki/Taraz" title="Taraz">Taraz</a> (Aulie-Ata) and <a href="/wiki/Hazrat-e_Turkestan" class="mw-redirect" title="Hazrat-e Turkestan">Hazrat-e Turkestan</a> had long served as important way-stations along the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> connecting Asia and Europe, true political consolidation began only with the Mongol rule of the early 13th century. Under the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a>, the largest in world history, administrative districts were established. These eventually came under the rule of the emergent <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Khanate" title="Kazakh Khanate">Kazakh Khanate</a> (Kazakhstan). </p>
      <p>Throughout this period, traditional <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> life and a livestock-based economy continued to dominate the <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a>. In the 15th century, a distinct <a href="/wiki/Kazakhs" title="Kazakhs">Kazakh</a> identity began to emerge among the <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> tribes. This was followed by the <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_War_of_Independence" title="Kazakh War of Independence">Kazakh War of Independence</a> where the khanate gained its sovereignty from the <a href="/wiki/Shaybanids" title="Shaybanids">Shaybanids</a>. The process was consolidated by the mid-16th century with the appearance of the <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_language" title="Kazakh language">Kazakh language</a>, culture, and economy. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%96%D1%83%D0%B7.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/%D0%96%D1%83%D0%B7.svg/250px-%D0%96%D1%83%D0%B7.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/%D0%96%D1%83%D0%B7.svg/375px-%D0%96%D1%83%D0%B7.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/%D0%96%D1%83%D0%B7.svg/500px-%D0%96%D1%83%D0%B7.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="658" data-file-height="369"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%96%D1%83%D0%B7.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Approximate areas occupied by the three Kazakh jüz in the early 20th century. 
         <table> 
          <tbody>
           <tr> 
            <td><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
             <div class="legend">
              <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#ccff99; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Junior_juz" class="mw-redirect" title="Junior juz">Junior juz</a>
             </div> </td> 
            <td>
             <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
             <div class="legend">
              <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#fdd99b; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Middle_Juz" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Juz">Middle Juz</a>
             </div> </td> 
            <td>
             <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
             <div class="legend">
              <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#ffaaaa; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Great_juz" class="mw-redirect" title="Great juz">Great juz</a>
             </div> </td>
           </tr>
          </tbody>
         </table>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Nevertheless, the region was the focus of ever-increasing disputes between the native Kazakh <a href="/wiki/Emir" title="Emir">emirs</a> and the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Persian-speaking_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian-speaking peoples">Persian-speaking peoples</a> to the south. At its height, the Khanate would rule parts of Central Asia and control <a href="/wiki/Cumania" title="Cumania">Cumania</a>. By the early 17th century, the Kazakh Khanate was struggling with the impact of tribal rivalries, which had effectively divided the population into the Great, Middle and Little (or Small) hordes (<i><a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCz" class="mw-redirect" title="Jüz">jüz</a></i>). Political disunion, tribal rivalries, and the diminishing importance of overland trade routes between east and west weakened the Kazakh Khanate. <a href="/wiki/Khiva_Khanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Khiva Khanate">Khiva Khanate</a> used this opportunity and annexed <a href="/wiki/Mangyshlak_Peninsula" title="Mangyshlak Peninsula">Mangyshlak Peninsula</a>. Uzbek rule there lasted two centuries until the Russian arrival. </p>
      <p>During the 17th century, the Kazakhs fought <a href="/wiki/Oirats" title="Oirats">Oirats</a>, a federation of western <a href="/wiki/Mongol" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol">Mongol</a> tribes, including the <a href="/wiki/Dzungar_people" title="Dzungar people">Dzungar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[24]</a></sup> The beginning of the 18th century marked the zenith of the Kazakh Khanate. During this period the Little Horde participated in the 1723–1730 <a href="/wiki/Kazakh-Dzungar_Wars" title="Kazakh-Dzungar Wars">war against the Dzungar Khanate</a>, following their "Great Disaster" <a href="/wiki/Invasion" title="Invasion">invasion</a> of Kazakh territories. Under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Abul_Khair_Khan" title="Abul Khair Khan">Abul Khair Khan</a>, the Kazakh won major victories over the Dzungar at the Bulanty River in 1726, and at the Battle of Anrakay in 1729.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ablai_Khan" title="Ablai Khan">Ablai Khan</a> participated in the most significant battles against the Dzungar from the 1720s to the 1750s, for which he was declared a "<i>batyr</i>" ("hero") by the people. The Kazakh suffered from the frequent raids against them by the Volga <a href="/wiki/Kalmyk_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalmyk people">Kalmyk</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kokand_Khanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Kokand Khanate">Kokand Khanate</a> used the weakness of Kazakh jüzs after Dzungar and Kalmyk raids and conquered present Southeastern Kazakhstan, including <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, the formal capital in the first quarter of the 19th century. Also, the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Bukhara" title="Emirate of Bukhara">Emirate of Bukhara</a> ruled <a href="/wiki/Shymkent" title="Shymkent">Shymkent</a> before the Russians took dominance.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_Empire">Russian Empire</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Battle_Cossacks_with_Kyrgyz_1826.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Battle_Cossacks_with_Kyrgyz_1826.JPG/220px-Battle_Cossacks_with_Kyrgyz_1826.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Battle_Cossacks_with_Kyrgyz_1826.JPG/330px-Battle_Cossacks_with_Kyrgyz_1826.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Battle_Cossacks_with_Kyrgyz_1826.JPG/440px-Battle_Cossacks_with_Kyrgyz_1826.JPG 2x" data-file-width="759" data-file-height="516"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Battle_Cossacks_with_Kyrgyz_1826.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ural_Cossacks" title="Ural Cossacks">Ural Cossacks</a> skirmish with <a href="/wiki/Kazakhs" title="Kazakhs">Kazakhs</a> (the Russians originally called the Kazakhs "Kirgiz")
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the first half of the 18th century, the Russian Empire constructed the Irtysh line, a series of forty-six forts and ninety-six redoubts, including <a href="/wiki/Omsk" title="Omsk">Omsk</a> (1716), <a href="/wiki/Semey" title="Semey">Semipalatinsk</a> (1718), <a href="/wiki/Pavlodar" title="Pavlodar">Pavlodar</a> (1720), <a href="/wiki/Orenburg" title="Orenburg">Orenburg</a> (1743) and <a href="/wiki/Petropavl" title="Petropavl">Petropavlovsk</a> (1752),<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[27]</a></sup> to prevent Kazakh and Oirat raids into Russian territory.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[28]</a></sup> In the late 18th century the Kazakhs took advantage of <a href="/wiki/Pugachev%27s_Rebellion" title="Pugachev's Rebellion">Pugachev's Rebellion</a>, which was centred on the Volga area, to raid Russian and <a href="/wiki/Volga_Germans" title="Volga Germans">Volga German</a> settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[29]</a></sup> In the 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> began to expand its influence into Central Asia. The "<a href="/wiki/Great_Game" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Game">Great Game</a>" period is generally regarded as running from approximately 1813 to the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Russian_Convention_of_1907" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Russian Convention of 1907">Anglo-Russian Convention of 1907</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">tsars</a> effectively ruled over most of the territory belonging to what is now the Republic of Kazakhstan. </p>
      <p>The Russian Empire introduced a system of administration and built military garrisons and barracks in its effort to establish a presence in Central Asia in the so-called "Great Game" for dominance in the area against the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, which was extending its influence from the south in India and Southeast Asia. Russia built its first outpost, <a href="/wiki/Orsk" title="Orsk">Orsk</a>, in 1735. Russia introduced the Russian language in all schools and governmental organisations. </p>
      <p>Russian efforts to impose its system aroused the resentment by the <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazakh people">Kazakh people</a>, and, by the 1860s, some Kazakhs resisted Russia's rule. It had disrupted the traditional nomadic lifestyle and livestock-based economy, and people were suffering from hunger and starvation, with some Kazakh tribes being decimated. The Kazakh national movement, which began in the late 19th century, sought to preserve the native language and identity by resisting the attempts of the Russian Empire to assimilate and stifle them. </p>
      <p>From the 1890s onward, ever-larger numbers of settlers from the Russian Empire began <a href="/wiki/Colonising" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonising">colonising</a> the territory of present-day Kazakhstan, in particular, the province of <a href="/wiki/Semirechye" class="mw-redirect" title="Semirechye">Semirechye</a>. The number of settlers rose still further once the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Aral_Railway" title="Trans-Aral Railway">Trans-Aral Railway</a> from <a href="/wiki/Orenburg" title="Orenburg">Orenburg</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tashkent" title="Tashkent">Tashkent</a> was completed in 1906. A specially created Migration Department (Переселенческое Управление) in <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a> oversaw and encouraged the migration to expand Russian influence in the area. During the 19th century about 400,000 Russians immigrated to Kazakhstan, and about one million Slavs, Germans, Jews, and others immigrated to the region during the first third of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vasile_Balabanov" class="mw-redirect" title="Vasile Balabanov">Vasile Balabanov</a> was the administrator responsible for the resettlement during much of this time. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Alikhan_Bukeikhanov.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Alikhan_Bukeikhanov.jpg/150px-Alikhan_Bukeikhanov.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Alikhan_Bukeikhanov.jpg/225px-Alikhan_Bukeikhanov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Alikhan_Bukeikhanov.jpg/300px-Alikhan_Bukeikhanov.jpg 2x" data-file-width="338" data-file-height="474"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Alikhan_Bukeikhanov.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Alikhan_Bukeikhanov" title="Alikhan Bukeikhanov">Alikhan Bukeikhanov</a>, a Kazakh statesman who served as the Prime Minister of the <a href="/wiki/Alash_Autonomy" title="Alash Autonomy">Alash Autonomy</a> from 1917 to 1920
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The competition for land and water that ensued between the Kazakh and the newcomers caused great resentment against colonial rule during the final years of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>. The most serious uprising, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Asian Revolt">Central Asian Revolt</a>, occurred in 1916. The Kazakh attacked Russian and <a href="/wiki/Cossack" class="mw-redirect" title="Cossack">Cossack</a> settlers and military garrisons. The revolt resulted in a series of clashes and in brutal massacres committed by both sides.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[31]</a></sup> Both sides resisted the communist government until late 1919. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_Union">Soviet Union</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic">Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stanitsa_Sofiiskaya.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c5/Stanitsa_Sofiiskaya.jpg/220px-Stanitsa_Sofiiskaya.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c5/Stanitsa_Sofiiskaya.jpg/330px-Stanitsa_Sofiiskaya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c5/Stanitsa_Sofiiskaya.jpg/440px-Stanitsa_Sofiiskaya.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="561"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stanitsa_Sofiiskaya.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Stanitsa Sofiiskaya, <a href="/wiki/Talgar" title="Talgar">Talgar</a>. 1920s
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Young_Pioneers_in_Kazakh_SSR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Young_Pioneers_in_Kazakh_SSR.jpg/220px-Young_Pioneers_in_Kazakh_SSR.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Young_Pioneers_in_Kazakh_SSR.jpg/330px-Young_Pioneers_in_Kazakh_SSR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Young_Pioneers_in_Kazakh_SSR.jpg/440px-Young_Pioneers_in_Kazakh_SSR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="762"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Young_Pioneers_in_Kazakh_SSR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Young_Pioneer_organization_of_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Pioneer organization of the Soviet Union">Young Pioneers</a> at a Young Pioneer camp in Kazakh SSR
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Following the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">collapse of central government</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Petrograd</a> in November 1917, the Kazakhs (then in Russia officially referred to as "Kirghiz") experienced a brief period of <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_entity" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous entity">autonomy</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Alash_Autonomy" title="Alash Autonomy">Alash Autonomy</a>) to eventually succumb to the <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik">Bolsheviks</a>′ rule. On 26 August 1920, the <a href="/wiki/Kirghiz_Autonomous_Socialist_Soviet_Republic_(1920%E2%80%9325)" title="Kirghiz Autonomous Socialist Soviet Republic (1920–25)">Kirghiz Autonomous Socialist Soviet Republic</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic</a> (RSFSR) was established. The Kirghiz ASSR included the territory of present-day Kazakhstan, but its administrative centre was a mainly Russian-populated town of <a href="/wiki/Orenburg" title="Orenburg">Orenburg</a>. In June 1925, the Kirghiz ASSR was renamed the <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazakh Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Kazak ASSR</a> and its administrative centre was transferred to the town of <a href="/wiki/Kyzylorda" title="Kyzylorda">Kyzylorda</a>, and in April 1927 to <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Alma-Ata</a>. </p>
      <p>Soviet repression of the traditional elite, along with forced <a href="/wiki/Collectivisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collectivisation">collectivisation</a> in the late 1920s and 1930s, brought <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a> and high fatalities, leading to unrest (see also: <a href="/wiki/Famine_in_Kazakhstan_of_1932%E2%80%9333" class="mw-redirect" title="Famine in Kazakhstan of 1932–33">Famine in Kazakhstan of 1932–33</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[33]</a></sup> During the 1930s, some members of the Kazakh cultured society were executed – as part of the <a href="/wiki/Political_repression_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Political repression in the Soviet Union">policies of political reprisals</a> pursued by the Soviet government in Moscow. </p>
      <p>On 5 December 1936, the <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazakh Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Kazakh Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a> (whose territory by then corresponded to that of modern Kazakhstan) was detached from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic</a> (RSFSR) and made the <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic">Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic</a>, a full <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">union republic</a> of the USSR, one of eleven such republics at the time, along with the <a href="/wiki/Kirghiz_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Kirghiz Soviet Socialist Republic">Kirghiz Soviet Socialist Republic</a>. </p>
      <p>The republic was one of the destinations for exiled and convicted persons, as well as for mass resettlements, or deportations affected by the central USSR authorities during the 1930s and 1940s, such as approximately 400,000 <a href="/wiki/Volga_Germans" title="Volga Germans">Volga Germans</a> deported from the <a href="/wiki/Volga_German_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Volga German Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Volga German Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a> in September–October 1941, and then later the <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_Kazakhstan" title="Greeks in Kazakhstan">Greeks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deportation_of_the_Crimean_Tatars" title="Deportation of the Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a>. Deportees and prisoners were interned in some of the biggest <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">Soviet labour camps</a> (the Gulag), including <a href="/wiki/Akmol" title="Akmol">ALZhIR</a> camp outside Astana, which was reserved for the wives of men considered "enemies of the people".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[34]</a></sup> Many moved due to the policy of <a href="/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Population transfer in the Soviet Union">population transfer in the Soviet Union</a> and others were forced into <a href="/wiki/Involuntary_settlements_in_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Involuntary settlements in the Soviet Union">involuntary settlements in the Soviet Union</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:International_conference_on_Primary_Health_Care_-_Conferencia_Internacional_sobre_Atenci%C3%B3n_Primaria_de_Salud_-_Almaty_-1978.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/International_conference_on_Primary_Health_Care_-_Conferencia_Internacional_sobre_Atenci%C3%B3n_Primaria_de_Salud_-_Almaty_-1978.jpg/220px-International_conference_on_Primary_Health_Care_-_Conferencia_Internacional_sobre_Atenci%C3%B3n_Primaria_de_Salud_-_Almaty_-1978.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/International_conference_on_Primary_Health_Care_-_Conferencia_Internacional_sobre_Atenci%C3%B3n_Primaria_de_Salud_-_Almaty_-1978.jpg/330px-International_conference_on_Primary_Health_Care_-_Conferencia_Internacional_sobre_Atenci%C3%B3n_Primaria_de_Salud_-_Almaty_-1978.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fd/International_conference_on_Primary_Health_Care_-_Conferencia_Internacional_sobre_Atenci%C3%B3n_Primaria_de_Salud_-_Almaty_-1978.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="282"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:International_conference_on_Primary_Health_Care_-_Conferencia_Internacional_sobre_Atenci%C3%B3n_Primaria_de_Salud_-_Almaty_-1978.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The International Conference on Primary Health Care in 1978, known as the <a href="/wiki/Alma_Ata_Declaration" title="Alma Ata Declaration">Alma-Ata Declaration</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Soviet-German War</a> (1941–1945) led to an increase in industrialisation and <a href="/wiki/Mineral_extraction" class="mw-redirect" title="Mineral extraction">mineral extraction</a> in support of the war effort. At the time of the USSR's leader <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>'s death in 1953, however, Kazakhstan still had an overwhelmingly agricultural economy. In 1953, Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> initiated the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Lands_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin Lands Campaign">Virgin Lands Campaign</a> designed to turn the traditional pasturelands of Kazakhstan into a major grain-producing region for the Soviet Union. The Virgin Lands policy brought mixed results. However, along with later modernisations under Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev" title="Leonid Brezhnev">Leonid Brezhnev</a> (in power 1964–1982), it accelerated the development of the agricultural sector, which remains the source of livelihood for a large percentage of Kazakhstan's population. Because of the decades of privation, war and resettlement, by 1959 the <a href="/wiki/Kazakhs" title="Kazakhs">Kazakh</a> had become a minority in the country, making up 30% of the population. Ethnic <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> accounted for 43%.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1947, the USSR government, as part of its <a href="/wiki/Soviet_atomic_bomb_project" title="Soviet atomic bomb project">atomic bomb project</a>, founded an <a href="/wiki/Semipalatinsk_Test_Site" title="Semipalatinsk Test Site">atomic bomb test site</a> near the north-eastern town of <a href="/wiki/Semey" title="Semey">Semipalatinsk</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/RDS-1" title="RDS-1">first Soviet nuclear bomb</a> test was conducted in 1949. Hundreds of nuclear tests were conducted until 1989 and had negative ecological and biological consequences.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[36]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Anti-nuclear_movement_in_Kazakhstan" title="Anti-nuclear movement in Kazakhstan">Anti-nuclear movement in Kazakhstan</a> became a major political force in the late 1980s. </p>
      <p>In December 1986, mass demonstrations by young ethnic Kazakhs, later called the <a href="/wiki/Jeltoqsan" title="Jeltoqsan">Jeltoqsan</a> riot, took place in Almaty to protest the replacement of the <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary" class="mw-redirect" title="General Secretary">First Secretary</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Kazakhstan" title="Communist Party of Kazakhstan">Communist Party</a> of the Kazakh SSR <a href="/wiki/Dinmukhamed_Konayev" class="mw-redirect" title="Dinmukhamed Konayev">Dinmukhamed Konayev</a> with <a href="/wiki/Gennady_Kolbin" title="Gennady Kolbin">Gennady Kolbin</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_SFSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian SFSR">Russian SFSR</a>. Governmental troops suppressed the unrest, several people were killed, and many demonstrators were jailed.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[37]</a></sup> In the waning days of Soviet rule, discontent continued to grow and found expression under Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>'s policy of <i><a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">glasnost</a></i>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span></h3> 
      <p><span class="anchor" id="Independence"></span> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Monument_of_Independence,_Republic_Square,_Almaty.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Monument_of_Independence%2C_Republic_Square%2C_Almaty.jpg/150px-Monument_of_Independence%2C_Republic_Square%2C_Almaty.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Monument_of_Independence%2C_Republic_Square%2C_Almaty.jpg/225px-Monument_of_Independence%2C_Republic_Square%2C_Almaty.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Monument_of_Independence%2C_Republic_Square%2C_Almaty.jpg/300px-Monument_of_Independence%2C_Republic_Square%2C_Almaty.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2105" data-file-height="2897"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Monument_of_Independence,_Republic_Square,_Almaty.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Monument of Independence, Republic Square, Almaty
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 25 October 1990, Kazakhstan declared its <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> on its territory as a republic within the Soviet Union. Following the August 1991 aborted <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt">coup attempt</a> in Moscow, Kazakhstan declared <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstani_Independence_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazakhstani Independence Day">independence</a> on 16 December 1991, thus becoming the last Soviet republic to declare independence. Ten days later, the Soviet Union itself <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">ceased to exist</a>. </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan's communist-era leader, <a href="/wiki/Nursultan_Nazarbayev" title="Nursultan Nazarbayev">Nursultan Nazarbayev</a>, became the country's first President. Nazarbayev ruled in an authoritarian manner. Emphasis was on converting the country's economy to a market economy while political reforms lagged behind achievements in the economy. By 2006, Kazakhstan generated 60% of the GDP of Central Asia, primarily through its oil industry.<sup id="cite_ref-time_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time-21">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1997, the government moved the capital to <a href="/wiki/Astana" class="mw-redirect" title="Astana">Astana</a>, renamed Nur-Sultan on 23 March 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[38]</a></sup> from <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, Kazakhstan's largest city, where it had been established under the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Kazakhstan" title="Geography of Kazakhstan">Geography of Kazakhstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Kazakhstan" title="List of cities in Kazakhstan">List of cities in Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kazakhstan_BMNG.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Kazakhstan_BMNG.jpg/220px-Kazakhstan_BMNG.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Kazakhstan_BMNG.jpg/330px-Kazakhstan_BMNG.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Kazakhstan_BMNG.jpg/440px-Kazakhstan_BMNG.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3803" data-file-height="2179"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kazakhstan_BMNG.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Satellite image of Kazakhstan (November 2004)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As it extends across both sides of the <a href="/wiki/Ural_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ural River">Ural River</a>, considered the dividing line with the European continent, Kazakhstan is one of only two <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked countries</a> in the world that <a href="/wiki/Transcontinental_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Transcontinental countries">has territory in two continents</a> (the other is <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>). </p>
      <p>With an area of 2,700,000 square kilometres (1,000,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi)&nbsp;– equivalent in size to Western Europe&nbsp;– Kazakhstan is the ninth-largest country and largest landlocked country in the world. While it was part of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, Kazakhstan lost some of its territory to China's <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> province,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[40]</a></sup> and some to Uzbekistan's <a href="/wiki/Karakalpakstan" title="Karakalpakstan">Karakalpakstan</a> autonomous republic during Soviet years. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%BE_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%BE_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%BE_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="95" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%BE_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%BE_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%BE_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%BE_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3800" data-file-height="1647"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%BE_%D0%BE%D1%82_%D0%BF%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The mountainous <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tian Shan</a> region of south-eastern Kazakhstan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Eurasian_steppe_belt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Eurasian_steppe_belt.jpg/220px-Eurasian_steppe_belt.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Eurasian_steppe_belt.jpg/330px-Eurasian_steppe_belt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Eurasian_steppe_belt.jpg/440px-Eurasian_steppe_belt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1529"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Eurasian_steppe_belt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Steppe" title="Kazakh Steppe">Kazakh Steppe</a> is part of the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Steppe" title="Eurasian Steppe">Eurasian Steppe</a> Belt (in <span style="display:inline-block;width:1em;height:1em;border:1.62px solid black;background:#AAEEFF;" title="#aaeeff"> </span> on the map)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>It shares borders of 6,846 kilometres (4,254&nbsp;mi) with Russia, 2,203 kilometres (1,369&nbsp;mi) with <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>, 1,533 kilometres (953&nbsp;mi) with China, 1,051 kilometres (653&nbsp;mi) with <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a>, and 379 kilometres (235&nbsp;mi) with <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>. Major cities include <a href="/wiki/Nur-Sultan" title="Nur-Sultan">Nur-Sultan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karagandy" class="mw-redirect" title="Karagandy">Karagandy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shymkent" title="Shymkent">Shymkent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atyrau" title="Atyrau">Atyrau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oskemen" title="Oskemen">Oskemen</a>. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/40th_parallel_north" title="40th parallel north">40°</a> and <a href="/wiki/56th_parallel_north" title="56th parallel north">56° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/46th_meridian_east" title="46th meridian east">46°</a> and <a href="/wiki/88th_meridian_east" title="88th meridian east">88° E</a>. While located primarily in Asia, a small portion of Kazakhstan is also located west of the <a href="/wiki/Urals" class="mw-redirect" title="Urals">Urals</a> in Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan's terrain extends west to east from the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Altay_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Altay Mountains">Altay Mountains</a> and north to south from the plains of <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Western Siberia</a> to the oases and deserts of Central Asia. The <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Steppe" title="Kazakh Steppe">Kazakh Steppe</a> (plain), with an area of around 804,500 square kilometres (310,600&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), occupies one-third of the country and is the world's largest dry <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a> region. The steppe is characterised by large areas of <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grasslands</a> and sandy regions. Major seas, lakes and rivers include <a href="/wiki/Lake_Balkhash" title="Lake Balkhash">Lake Balkhash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Zaysan" title="Lake Zaysan">Lake Zaysan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Charyn_Canyon" title="Charyn Canyon">Charyn River and gorge</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ili_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ili River">Ili</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irtysh_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Irtysh River">Irtysh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ishim_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ishim River">Ishim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ural_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ural River">Ural</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syr_Darya" title="Syr Darya">Syr Darya</a> rivers, and the <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral Sea</a> until it largely dried up in one of the world's worst environmental disasters.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Charyn_Canyon" title="Charyn Canyon">Charyn Canyon</a> is 80 kilometres (50&nbsp;mi) long, cutting through a red <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> plateau and stretching along the Charyn River gorge in northern <a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tian Shan</a> ("Heavenly Mountains", 200&nbsp;km (124&nbsp;mi) east of Almaty) at 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r994658806"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Kazakhstan&amp;params=43_21_1.16_N_79_4_49.28_E_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">43°21′1.16″N</span> <span class="longitude">79°4′49.28″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">43.3503222°N 79.0803556°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">43.3503222; 79.0803556</span></span></span></a></span>. The steep canyon slopes, columns and arches rise to heights of between 150 and 300 metres (490 and 980 feet). The inaccessibility of the canyon provided a safe haven for a rare <a href="/wiki/Ash_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Ash tree">ash tree</a>, <i>Fraxinus sogdiana</i>, which survived the <a href="/wiki/Ice_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Ice Age">Ice Age</a> there and has now also grown in some other areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Bigach_crater" title="Bigach crater">Bigach crater</a>, at 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r994658806"><span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Kazakhstan&amp;params=48_30_N_82_00_E_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">48°30′N</span> <span class="longitude">82°00′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">48.500°N 82.000°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">48.500; 82.000</span></span></span></a></span>, is a <a href="/wiki/Pliocene" title="Pliocene">Pliocene</a> or <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a> <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">asteroid</a> <a href="/wiki/Impact_crater" title="Impact crater">impact crater</a>, 8&nbsp;km (5&nbsp;mi) in diameter and estimated to be 5±3&nbsp;million years old. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">Natural resources</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_policy_of_Kazakhstan" title="Energy policy of Kazakhstan">Energy policy of Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kazakhstan has an abundant supply of accessible mineral and fossil fuel resources. Development of petroleum, natural gas, and mineral extractions has attracted most of the over $40&nbsp;billion in foreign investment in Kazakhstan since 1993 and accounts for some 57% of the nation's industrial output (or approximately 13% of gross domestic product). According to some estimates,<sup id="cite_ref-Homestead_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Homestead-49">[43]</a></sup> Kazakhstan has the second largest <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chromium" title="Chromium">chromium</a>, lead, and <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a> reserves; the third largest <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a> reserves; the fifth largest copper reserves; and ranks in the top ten for coal, iron, and gold. It is also an exporter of diamonds. Perhaps most significant for economic development, Kazakhstan also currently has the 11th largest proven reserves of both petroleum and natural gas.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In total, there are 160 deposits with over 2.7&nbsp;billion tonnes (2.7&nbsp;billion long tons) of petroleum. Oil explorations have shown that the deposits on the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_sea" class="mw-redirect" title="Caspian sea">Caspian shore</a> are only a small part of a much larger deposit. It is said that 3.5&nbsp;billion tonnes (3.4&nbsp;billion long tons) of oil and 2.5&nbsp;billion cubic metres (88&nbsp;billion cubic feet) of gas could be found in that area. Overall the estimate of Kazakhstan's oil deposits is 6.1&nbsp;billion tonnes (6.0&nbsp;billion long tons). However, there are only three <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">refineries</a> within the country, situated in <a href="/wiki/Atirau" class="mw-redirect" title="Atirau">Atyrau</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[45]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pavlodar" title="Pavlodar">Pavlodar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shymkent" title="Shymkent">Shymkent</a>. These are not capable of processing the total crude output, so much of it is exported to Russia. According to the US <a href="/wiki/Energy_Information_Administration" title="Energy Information Administration">Energy Information Administration</a> Kazakhstan was producing approximately 1,540,000 barrels (245,000&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>) of oil per day in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan also possesses large deposits of phosphorite. One of the largest known being the Karatau basin with 650 million tonnes of P2O5 and Chilisai deposit of <a href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%90%D0%BA%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%B1%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%B9%D0%BD" class="extiw" title="ru:Актобинский фосфоритоносный бассейн">Aqtobe phosphorite basin</a> located in north western Kazakhstan, with a resource of 500–800&nbsp;million tonnes of 9% ore.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 17 October 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Extractive_Industries_Transparency_Initiative" title="Extractive Industries Transparency Initiative">Extractive Industries Transparency Initiative</a> (EITI) accepted Kazakhstan as "EITI Compliant", meaning that the country has a basic and functional process to ensure the regular disclosure of natural resource revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[49]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kazakhstan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Kazakhstan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Kazakhstan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Kazakhstan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Kazakhstan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Kazakhstan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Kazakhstan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kazakhstan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Kazakhstan map of Köppen climate classification
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kazakhstan has an "extreme" <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a>, with warm summers and very cold winters. Indeed, Nursultan is the second coldest capital city in the world after <a href="/wiki/Ulaanbaatar" title="Ulaanbaatar">Ulaanbaatar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> varies between arid and semi-arid conditions, the winter being particularly dry.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[50]</a></sup> </p>
