      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Kazakhstan" title="Wildlife of Kazakhstan">Wildlife of Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vulpes_corsac.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Vulpes_corsac.jpg/170px-Vulpes_corsac.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Vulpes_corsac.jpg/255px-Vulpes_corsac.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Vulpes_corsac.jpg/340px-Vulpes_corsac.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1994" data-file-height="2935"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vulpes_corsac.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Corsac_fox" title="Corsac fox">Corsac fox</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are ten <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Kazakhstan" title="List of protected areas of Kazakhstan">nature reserves</a> and ten <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_Kazakhstan" title="List of national parks of Kazakhstan">national parks</a> in Kazakhstan that provide safe haven for many rare and endangered plants and animals. Common plants are <i><a href="/wiki/Astragalus" title="Astragalus">Astragalus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gagea" title="Gagea">Gagea</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Allium" title="Allium">Allium</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Carex" title="Carex">Carex</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Oxytropis" title="Oxytropis">Oxytropis</a></i>; endangered plant species include native wild apple (<i><a href="/wiki/Malus_sieversii" title="Malus sieversii">Malus sieversii</a></i>), wild grape (<i><a href="/wiki/Vitis_vinifera" title="Vitis vinifera">Vitis vinifera</a></i>) and several wild <a href="/wiki/Tulip" title="Tulip">tulip</a> species (e.g., <i><a href="/wiki/Tulipa_greigii" title="Tulipa greigii">Tulipa greigii</a></i>) and rare onion species <i><a href="/wiki/Allium_karataviense" title="Allium karataviense">Allium karataviense</a></i>, also <i><a href="/wiki/Iris_willmottiana" title="Iris willmottiana">Iris willmottiana</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Tulipa_kaufmanniana" title="Tulipa kaufmanniana">Tulipa kaufmanniana</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[53]</a></sup> Kazakhstan had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 8.23/10, ranking it 26th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-60">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Common mammals include the <a href="/wiki/Wolf" title="Wolf">wolf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">red fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corsac_fox" title="Corsac fox">corsac fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moose" title="Moose">moose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argali" title="Argali">argali</a> (the largest species of sheep), <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_lynx" title="Eurasian lynx">Eurasian lynx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pallas%27s_cat" title="Pallas's cat">Pallas's cat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Snow_leopards" class="mw-redirect" title="Snow leopards">snow leopards</a>, several of which are protected. Kazakhstan's Red Book of Protected Species lists 125 vertebrates including many birds and mammals, and 404 plants including fungi, algae and lichen.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Kazakhstan" title="Government of Kazakhstan">Government of Kazakhstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Kazakhstan" title="Politics of Kazakhstan">Politics of Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_system">Political system</span></h3> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:left; float:left; margin-right:9px; margin-left:2px;"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_(2019-11-07)_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Kassym-Jomart Tokayev (2019-11-07) 01.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_%282019-11-07%29_01.jpg/120px-Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_%282019-11-07%29_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="169" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_%282019-11-07%29_01.jpg/180px-Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_%282019-11-07%29_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_%282019-11-07%29_01.jpg/240px-Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_%282019-11-07%29_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="372" data-file-height="524"></a> </td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%A3%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Аскар Узакпаевич Мамин.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/%D0%90%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%A3%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD.jpg/120px-%D0%90%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%A3%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="169" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/%D0%90%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%A3%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD.jpg/180px-%D0%90%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%A3%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/%D0%90%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%A3%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD.jpg/240px-%D0%90%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%A3%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87_%D0%9C%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD.jpg 2x" data-file-width="728" data-file-height="1024"></a> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev" title="Kassym-Jomart Tokayev">Kassym-Jomart Tokayev</a><br><small><a href="/wiki/President_of_Kazakhstan" title="President of Kazakhstan">President</a></small> </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Askar_Mamin" title="Askar Mamin">Askar Mamin</a><br><small><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Kazakhstan" title="Prime Minister of Kazakhstan">Prime Minister</a></small> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Kazakhstan is a democratic, secular, constitutional <a href="/wiki/Unitary_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Unitary republic">unitary republic</a>; <a href="/wiki/Nursultan_Nazarbayev" title="Nursultan Nazarbayev">Nursultan Nazarbayev</a> led the country from 1991 to 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[57]</a></sup> He was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev" title="Kassym-Jomart Tokayev">Kassym-Jomart Tokayev</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tokayev-wins_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tokayev-wins-65">[59]</a></sup> The president may veto legislation that has been passed by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Kazakhstan" title="Parliament of Kazakhstan">parliament</a> and is also the <a href="/wiki/Commander_in_chief" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander in chief">commander in chief</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Republic_of_Kazakhstan" title="Armed Forces of the Republic of Kazakhstan">armed forces</a>. The prime minister chairs the cabinet of ministers and serves as Kazakhstan's head of government. There are three deputy prime ministers and sixteen ministers in the cabinet.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan has a <a href="/wiki/Bicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> parliament composed of the <i><a href="/wiki/Majilis" class="mw-redirect" title="Majilis">Majilis</a></i> (the <a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">lower house</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Kazakhstan" title="Senate of Kazakhstan">senate</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">upper house</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[61]</a></sup> Single-mandate districts popularly elect 107 seats in the <i>Majilis</i>; there also are ten members elected by party-list vote. The senate has 48 members. Two senators are selected by each of the elected assemblies (<a href="/wiki/M%C3%A4slihat" title="Mäslihat">mäslihats</a>) of Kazakhstan's sixteen principal <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Kazakhstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative divisions of Kazakhstan">administrative divisions</a> (fourteen regions plus the cities of Nur-Sultan, Almaty, and Shymkent). The president appoints the remaining fifteen senators. <i>Majilis</i> deputies and the government both have the right of legislative initiative, though the government proposes most legislation considered by the parliament. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_reforms">Political reforms</span></h3> 
      <p>Reforms have begun to be implemented after the election of Kassym-Jomart Tokayev in June 2019. Tokayev supports a culture of opposition, public assembly, and loosening rules on forming political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-poleform_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poleform-68">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In June 2019, on the initiative of the President of Kazakhstan, Kassym-Jomart Tokayev the National Council of Public Trust have been established as a platform in which wider society can discuss different views and strengthen the national conversation regarding government policies and reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-Iran_Daily_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iran_Daily-69">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In July 2019, the President of Kazakhstan announced a concept of a ‘listening state’ that quickly and efficiently responds to all constructive requests of the country's citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A law will be passed to allow representatives from other parties to hold Chair positions on some Parliamentary committees, to foster alternative views and opinions. The minimum membership threshold needed to register a political party will be reduced from 40,000 to 20,000 members.<sup id="cite_ref-Iran_Daily_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iran_Daily-69">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Special places for peaceful rallies in central areas will be allocated and a new draft law outlining the rights and obligations of organisers, participants and observers will be passed.<sup id="cite_ref-Iran_Daily_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iran_Daily-69">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In an effort to increase public safety, President Tokayev has strengthened the penalties for those who commit crimes against individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-Iran_Daily_69-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iran_Daily-69">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A0%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/%D0%A0%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-%D0%A0%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/%D0%A0%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-%D0%A0%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/%D0%A0%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-%D0%A0%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A0%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%BF%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D0%B0_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ak_Orda_Presidential_Palace" title="Ak Orda Presidential Palace">Ak Orda Presidential Palace</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Kazakhstan" title="Elections in Kazakhstan">Elections to the Majilis</a> in September 2004, yielded a lower house dominated by the pro-government <a href="/wiki/Nur-Otan" class="mw-redirect" title="Nur-Otan">Otan Party</a>, headed by President Nazarbayev. Two other parties considered sympathetic to the president, including the agrarian-industrial bloc AIST and the <a href="/wiki/Asar_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Asar Party">Asar Party</a>, founded by President Nazarbayev's daughter, won most of the remaining seats. The opposition parties which were officially registered and competed in the elections won a single seat. The Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe was monitoring the election, which it said fell short of international standards.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[65]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kazakh_Parliament_Astana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Kazakh_Parliament_Astana.jpg/220px-Kazakh_Parliament_Astana.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Kazakh_Parliament_Astana.jpg/330px-Kazakh_Parliament_Astana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Kazakh_Parliament_Astana.jpg/440px-Kazakh_Parliament_Astana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kazakh_Parliament_Astana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Kazakhstan" title="Parliament of Kazakhstan">Parliament of Kazakhstan</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nur_Otan_Astana.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Nur_Otan_Astana.JPG/220px-Nur_Otan_Astana.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Nur_Otan_Astana.JPG/330px-Nur_Otan_Astana.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Nur_Otan_Astana.JPG/440px-Nur_Otan_Astana.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nur_Otan_Astana.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Nur_Otan" title="Nur Otan">Nur Otan</a> Headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Nur-Sultan" title="Nur-Sultan">Nur-Sultan</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 4 December 2005, Nursultan Nazarbayev was re-elected in an apparent landslide victory. The electoral commission announced that he had won over 90% of the vote. The Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe (OSCE) concluded the election did not meet international standards despite some improvements in the administration of the election.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 17 August 2007, elections to the lower house of parliament were held and a coalition led by the ruling <a href="/wiki/Nur-Otan" class="mw-redirect" title="Nur-Otan">Nur-Otan</a> party, which included the <a href="/wiki/Asar_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Asar Party">Asar Party</a>, the Civil Party of Kazakhstan, and the <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_Party_of_Kazakhstan" title="Agrarian Party of Kazakhstan">Agrarian Party</a>, won every seat with 88% of the vote. None of the opposition parties has reached the benchmark 7% level of the seats. Opposition parties made accusations of serious irregularities in the election.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2010, president Nazarbayev rejected a call from supporters to hold a referendum to keep him in office until 2020. He insisted on presidential elections for a five-year term. In a vote held on 3 April 2011, president Nazarbayev received 95.54% of the vote with 89.9% of registered voters participating.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[69]</a></sup> In March 2011, Nazarbayev outlined the progress made toward democracy by Kazakhstan.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[70]</a></sup> As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kazakhstan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Kazakhstan was reported on the <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a> by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> as an <a href="/wiki/Authoritarian_regime" class="mw-redirect" title="Authoritarian regime">authoritarian regime</a>. </p>
      <p>On 26 April 2015, the fifth presidential election was held in Kazakhstan.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews2_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews2-77">[71]</a></sup> Nursultan Nazarbayev was re-elected with 97.7% of votes.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 19 March 2019, Nazarbayev announced his resignation from the presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[73]</a></sup> Kazakhstan's senate speaker <a href="/wiki/Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev" title="Kassym-Jomart Tokayev">Kassym-Jomart Tokayev</a> became acting president after Nursultan Nazarbayev's resignation.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[74]</a></sup> Later, Tokayev won the <a href="/wiki/2019_Kazakh_presidential_election" title="2019 Kazakh presidential election">2019 presidential election</a> that was held on 9 June.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[75]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Kazakhstan" title="Regions of Kazakhstan">Regions of Kazakhstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Kazakhstan" title="Districts of Kazakhstan">Districts of Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kazakhstan is divided into fourteen <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Kazakhstan" title="Regions of Kazakhstan">regions</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kazakh_language" title="Kazakh language">Kazakh</a>: <span lang="kk">облыстар</span>, <i lang="kk-Latn" title="Kazakh-language text">oblystar</i>; Russian: <span lang="ru">области</span>, <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language text">oblasti</i>). The regions are subdivided into 177 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Kazakhstan" title="Districts of Kazakhstan">districts</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kazakh_language" title="Kazakh language">Kazakh</a>: <span lang="kk">аудандар</span>, <i lang="kk-Latn" title="Kazakh-language text">aýdandar</i>; Russian: <span lang="ru">районы</span>, <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language text">rayony</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-82">[76]</a></sup> The districts are further subdivided into rural districts at the lowest level of administration, which include all rural settlements and villages without an associated municipal government.<sup id="cite_ref-Adilet_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adilet-83">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="special_status_cities"></span>The cities of <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nur-Sultan" title="Nur-Sultan">Nur-Sultan</a> have status "state importance" and do not belong to any region. The city of <a href="/wiki/Baikonur" title="Baikonur">Baikonur</a> has a special status because it is being leased until 2050 to Russia for the <a href="/wiki/Baikonur_cosmodrome" class="mw-redirect" title="Baikonur cosmodrome">Baikonur cosmodrome</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup> In June 2018 the city of <a href="/wiki/Shymkent" title="Shymkent">Shymkent</a> became a "city of republican significance".<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[78]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Each region is headed by an <a href="/wiki/Akim" title="Akim">äkim</a> (regional governor) appointed by the president. District <i>äkimi</i> are appointed by regional <i>akim</i>s. Kazakhstan's government relocated its capital from Almaty, established under the Soviet Union, to Astana on 10 December 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_divisions">Municipal divisions</span></h3> 
      <p>Municipalities exist at each level of administrative division in Kazakhstan. Cities of republican, regional, and district significance are designated as urban inhabited localities; all others are designated rural.<sup id="cite_ref-Adilet_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adilet-83">[77]</a></sup> At the highest level are the cities of Almaty and Nur-Sultan, which are classified as <i>cities of republican significance</i> on the administrative level equal to that of a region.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-82">[76]</a></sup> At the intermediate level are <i>cities of regional significance</i> on the administrative level equal to that of a district. Cities of these two levels may be divided into city districts.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-82">[76]</a></sup> At the lowest level are <i>cities of district significance</i>, and over two-thousand <i>villages and rural settlements</i> (<i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language text">aul</i>) on the administrative level equal to that of rural districts.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-82">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:The_map_of_Kazakhstan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/The_map_of_Kazakhstan.jpg/800px-The_map_of_Kazakhstan.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="461" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/The_map_of_Kazakhstan.jpg/1200px-The_map_of_Kazakhstan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/The_map_of_Kazakhstan.jpg/1600px-The_map_of_Kazakhstan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3471" data-file-height="1998"></a>

       </div>
      </div>
