      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Kazakhstan" title="Foreign relations of Kazakhstan">Foreign relations of Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kazakhstan is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Cooperation_Organization" title="Economic Cooperation Organization">Economic Cooperation Organization</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organization">Shanghai Cooperation Organization</a>. The nations of Kazakhstan, Russia, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, Kyrgyzstan and <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> established the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Community" title="Eurasian Economic Community">Eurasian Economic Community</a> in 2000, to revive earlier efforts to harmonise trade tariffs and to create a free trade zone under a customs union. On 1 December 2007, it was announced that Kazakhstan had been chosen to chair the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> for the year 2010. Kazakhstan was elected a member of the <a href="/wiki/UN_Human_Rights_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Human Rights Council">UN Human Rights Council</a> for the first time on 12 November 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[80]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan is also a member of the United Nations, <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Cooperation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe">Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Euro-Atlantic_Partnership_Council" title="Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council">Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkic_Council" title="Turkic Council">Turkic Council</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a> (OIC). It is an active participant in the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic Treaty Organization">North Atlantic Treaty Organisation</a> <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> program.<sup id="cite_ref-pfpsigs_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pfpsigs-87">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1999, Kazakhstan had applied for observer status at the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe_Parliamentary_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Europe Parliamentary Assembly">Council of Europe Parliamentary Assembly</a>. The official response of the Assembly was that because Kazakhstan is partially located in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[83]</a></sup> it could apply for full membership, but that it would not be granted any status whatsoever at the council until its democracy and human rights records improved. </p>
      <p>Since independence in 1991, Kazakhstan has pursued what is known as the "multivector foreign policy" (<a href="/wiki/Kazakh_language" title="Kazakh language">Kazakh</a>: <span lang="kk">көпвекторлы сыртқы саясат</span>), seeking equally good relations with its two large neighbours, Russia and China, as well as with the United States and the rest of the Western world.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[85]</a></sup> Russia currently leases approximately 6,000 square kilometres (2,317&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of territory enclosing the <a href="/wiki/Baikonur_Cosmodrome" title="Baikonur Cosmodrome">Baikonur Cosmodrome</a> space launch site in south central Kazakhstan, where the first man was launched into space as well as Soviet space shuttle <a href="/wiki/Buran_(spacecraft)" title="Buran (spacecraft)">Buran</a> and the well-known space station <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_and_Vladimir_Putin_(2019-04-03)_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_and_Vladimir_Putin_%282019-04-03%29_03.jpg/220px-Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_and_Vladimir_Putin_%282019-04-03%29_03.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_and_Vladimir_Putin_%282019-04-03%29_03.jpg/330px-Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_and_Vladimir_Putin_%282019-04-03%29_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_and_Vladimir_Putin_%282019-04-03%29_03.jpg/440px-Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_and_Vladimir_Putin_%282019-04-03%29_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev_and_Vladimir_Putin_(2019-04-03)_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>President <a href="/wiki/Kassym-Jomart_Tokayev" title="Kassym-Jomart Tokayev">Kassym-Jomart Tokayev</a> with president of Russia <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> in 2019
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 11 April 2010, presidents Nazarbayev and <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Obama</a> met at the Nuclear Security Summit in Washington, D.C., and discussed strengthening the strategic partnership between the United States and Kazakhstan. They pledged to intensify bilateral co-operation to promote nuclear safety and non-proliferation, regional stability in Central Asia, economic prosperity, and universal values.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In April 2011, president Obama called president Nazarbayev and discussed many cooperative efforts regarding nuclear security, including securing nuclear material from the BN-350 reactor. They reviewed progress on meeting goals that the two presidents established during their bilateral meeting at the Nuclear Security Summit in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[87]</a></sup> Since 2014 the Kazakhstani government has been bidding for a non-permanent member seat on the UN Security Council for 2017–2018.<sup id="cite_ref-AT5_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AT5-94">[88]</a></sup> On 28 June 2016 Kazakhstan was elected as a non-permanent member to serve on the UN Security Council for a two-year term.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-95">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Participants_in_the_SCO_Council_of_Heads_of_State_meeting_in_expanded_format,_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Participants_in_the_SCO_Council_of_Heads_of_State_meeting_in_expanded_format%2C_2017.jpg/220px-Participants_in_the_SCO_Council_of_Heads_of_State_meeting_in_expanded_format%2C_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Participants_in_the_SCO_Council_of_Heads_of_State_meeting_in_expanded_format%2C_2017.jpg/330px-Participants_in_the_SCO_Council_of_Heads_of_State_meeting_in_expanded_format%2C_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Participants_in_the_SCO_Council_of_Heads_of_State_meeting_in_expanded_format%2C_2017.jpg/440px-Participants_in_the_SCO_Council_of_Heads_of_State_meeting_in_expanded_format%2C_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Participants_in_the_SCO_Council_of_Heads_of_State_meeting_in_expanded_format,_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Nazarbayev and Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> during the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">SCO</a> Council of Heads of State meeting in Nur-Sultan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kazakhstan actively supports UN peacekeeping missions in Haiti, the Western Sahara, and Côte d'Ivoire.<sup id="cite_ref-TN1_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TN1-96">[90]</a></sup> In March 2014, the Ministry of Defense chose 20 Kazakhstani military men as observers for the UN peacekeeping missions. The military personnel, ranking from captain to colonel, had to go through a specialised UN training; they had to be fluent in English and skilled in using specialised military vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-TN1_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TN1-96">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2014, Kazakhstan gave Ukraine humanitarian aid during the conflict with Russian-backed rebels. In October 2014, Kazakhstan donated $30,000 to the International Committee of the Red Cross's humanitarian effort in Ukraine. In January 2015, to help the humanitarian crisis, Kazakhstan sent $400,000 of aid to <a href="/wiki/Novorossiya_(confederation)" title="Novorossiya (confederation)">Ukraine's southeastern regions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gpostukraine1_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gpostukraine1-97">[91]</a></sup> President Nazarbayev said of the war in Ukraine, "The fratricidal war has brought true devastation to eastern Ukraine, and it is a common task to stop the war there, strengthen Ukraine’s independence and secure territorial integrity of Ukraine."<sup id="cite_ref-ukrainenaz_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ukrainenaz-98">[92]</a></sup> Experts believe that no matter how the Ukraine crisis develops, Kazakhstan's relations with the European Union will remain normal.<sup id="cite_ref-CarnegieUkraniepiece_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CarnegieUkraniepiece-99">[93]</a></sup> It is believed that Nazarbayev's mediation is positively received by both Russia and Ukraine.<sup id="cite_ref-CarnegieUkraniepiece_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CarnegieUkraniepiece-99">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan's Ministry of Foreign Affairs released a statement on 26 January 2015: "We are firmly convinced that there is no alternative to peace negotiations as a way to resolve the crisis in south-eastern Ukraine."<sup id="cite_ref-ukrainejan26statement_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ukrainejan26statement-100">[94]</a></sup> In 2018, Kazakhstan signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><b>The Concept of the Foreign Policy of Kazakhstan for 2020–2023</b> </p>
      <p>On 6 March 2020, the Concept of the Foreign Policy of Kazakhstan for 2020–2030 was announced. The document outlines the following main points: </p>
      <p>– An open, predictable and consistent foreign policy of the country, which is progressive in nature and maintains its endurance by continuing the course of the First President – the country at a new stage of development; </p>
      <p>– Protection of human rights, development of humanitarian diplomacy and environmental protection; </p>
      <p>– Promotion of the country's economic interests in the international arena, including the implementation of state policy to attract investment; </p>
      <p>– Maintaining international peace and security; </p>
      <p>– Development of regional and multilateral diplomacy, which primarily involves strengthening mutually beneficial ties with key partners – Russia, China, the United States, Central Asian states and the EU countries, as well as through multilateral structures – the United Nations, the Organisation for Security and Cooperation in Europe, the Shanghai Cooperation Organisation, the Commonwealth of Independent States, and others.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[96]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Republic_of_Kazakhstan" title="Armed Forces of the Republic of Kazakhstan">Armed Forces of the Republic of Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kazakhstan_Republican_Guard.JPEG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Kazakhstan_Republican_Guard.JPEG/220px-Kazakhstan_Republican_Guard.JPEG" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Kazakhstan_Republican_Guard.JPEG/330px-Kazakhstan_Republican_Guard.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Kazakhstan_Republican_Guard.JPEG/440px-Kazakhstan_Republican_Guard.JPEG 2x" data-file-width="1563" data-file-height="827"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kazakhstan_Republican_Guard.JPEG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Republican_Guard_(Kazakhstan)" title="Republican Guard (Kazakhstan)">Kazakhstan Republican Guard</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:A_Kazakh_Sukhoi_Su-27P(modified).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/A_Kazakh_Sukhoi_Su-27P%28modified%29.jpg/220px-A_Kazakh_Sukhoi_Su-27P%28modified%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/A_Kazakh_Sukhoi_Su-27P%28modified%29.jpg/330px-A_Kazakh_Sukhoi_Su-27P%28modified%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/A_Kazakh_Sukhoi_Su-27P%28modified%29.jpg/440px-A_Kazakh_Sukhoi_Su-27P%28modified%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1314" data-file-height="811"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:A_Kazakh_Sukhoi_Su-27P(modified).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Kazakhstan <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-27" title="Sukhoi Su-27">Sukhoi Su-27</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Most of Kazakhstan's military was inherited from the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Armed_Forces" title="Soviet Armed Forces">Soviet Armed Forces</a>' <a href="/wiki/Turkestan_Military_District" title="Turkestan Military District">Turkestan Military District</a>. These units became the core of Kazakhstan's new military. It acquired all the units of the <a href="/wiki/40th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="40th Army (Soviet Union)">40th Army</a> (the former 32nd Army) and part of the 17th Army Corps, including six land-force divisions, storage bases, the 14th and 35th air-landing brigades, two rocket brigades, two artillery regiments, and a large amount of equipment that had been withdrawn from over the Urals after the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_Conventional_Armed_Forces_in_Europe" title="Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe">Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe</a>. Since the late 20th century, the Kazakhstan Army has focused on expanding the number of its armoured units. Since 1990, armoured units have expanded from 500 to 1,613 in 2005. </p>
      <p>The Kazakh air force is composed mostly of Soviet-era planes, including 41 <a href="/wiki/MiG-29" class="mw-redirect" title="MiG-29">MiG-29s</a>, 44 <a href="/wiki/MiG-31" class="mw-redirect" title="MiG-31">MiG-31s</a>, 37 <a href="/wiki/Su-24" class="mw-redirect" title="Su-24">Su-24s</a> and 60 <a href="/wiki/Su-27" class="mw-redirect" title="Su-27">Su-27s</a>. A small naval force is maintained on the Caspian Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[97]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan sent 29 military engineers to <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> to assist the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Iraq_(2003%E2%80%932011)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Iraq (2003–2011)">US post-invasion mission in Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[98]</a></sup> During the second Iraq War, Kazakhstani troops dismantled 4 million mines and other explosives, helped provide medical care to more than 5,000 coalition members and civilians, and purified 718 cubic metres (25,356&nbsp;cu&nbsp;ft) of water.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[99]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan's <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Committee_of_the_Republic_of_Kazakhstan" class="mw-redirect" title="National Security Committee of the Republic of Kazakhstan">National Security Committee</a> (UQK) was established on 13 June 1992. It includes the Service of Internal Security, Military Counterintelligence, Border Guard, several Commando units, and Foreign Intelligence (Barlau). The latter is considered as the most important part of KNB. Its director is <a href="/wiki/Nurtai_Abykayev" title="Nurtai Abykayev">Nurtai Abykayev</a>. </p>
      <p>Since 2002, the joint tactical peacekeeping exercise "Steppe Eagle" has been hosted by the Kazakhstan government. "Steppe Eagle" focuses on building coalitions and gives participating nations the opportunity to work together. During the Steppe Eagle exercises, the <a href="/wiki/KAZBAT" title="KAZBAT">KAZBAT</a> peacekeeping battalion operates within a multinational force under a unified command within multidisciplinary peacekeeping operations, with NATO and the US Military.<sup id="cite_ref-steppe1_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-steppe1-106">[100]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In December 2013, Kazakhstan announced it will send officers to support United Nations Peacekeeping forces in Haiti, Western Sahara, Ivory Coast and Liberia.<sup id="cite_ref-un1_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un1-107">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Kazakhstan" title="Human rights in Kazakhstan">Human rights in Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Kazakhstan's human rights situation is described as poor by independent observers. The 2015 <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> report on Kazakhstan said that the country "heavily restricts freedom of assembly, speech, and religion. In 2014, authorities closed newspapers, jailed or fined dozens of people after peaceful but unsanctioned protests, and fined or detained worshipers for practising religion outside state controls. Government critics, including opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Kozlov_(politician)" title="Vladimir Kozlov (politician)">Vladimir Kozlov</a>, remained in detention after unfair trials. In mid-2014, Kazakhstan adopted new criminal, criminal executive, criminal procedural, and administrative codes, and a new law on trade unions, which contain articles restricting fundamental freedoms and are incompatible with international standards. Torture remains common in places of detention."<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[102]</a></sup> However, Kazakhstan has achieved significant progress in reducing prison population.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[103]</a></sup> The 2016 Human Rights Watch report commented that Kazakhstan "took few meaningful steps to tackle a worsening human rights record in 2015, maintaining a focus on economic development over political reform."<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[104]</a></sup> Some critics of the government have been <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_misinformation#Combative_efforts" title="COVID-19 misinformation">arrested</a> for allegedly spreading <a href="/wiki/False_information" class="mw-redirect" title="False information">false information</a> about the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Kazakhstan" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Kazakhstan">COVID-19 pandemic in Kazakhstan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[105]</a></sup> Various police reforms, like creation of local police service and zero-tolerance policing, aimed at bringing police closer to local communities have not improved cooperation between police and ordinary citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> According to a US government report released in 2014, in Kazakhstan:</p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>"The law does not require police to inform detainees that they have the <a href="/wiki/Right_to_an_attorney" class="mw-redirect" title="Right to an attorney">right to an attorney</a>, and police did not do so. Human rights observers alleged that law enforcement officials dissuaded detainees from seeing an attorney, gathered evidence through preliminary questioning before a detainee’s attorney arrived, and in some cases used corrupt defense attorneys to gather evidence. [...]"<sup id="cite_ref-countryreport_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countryreport-113">[107]</a></sup> "The law does not adequately provide for an <a href="/wiki/Independent_judiciary" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent judiciary">independent judiciary</a>. The executive branch sharply limited judicial independence. Prosecutors enjoyed a quasi-judicial role and had the authority to suspend court decisions. Corruption was evident at every stage of the judicial process. Although judges were among the most highly paid government employees, lawyers and human rights monitors alleged that judges, prosecutors, and other officials solicited <a href="/wiki/Bribes" class="mw-redirect" title="Bribes">bribes</a> in exchange for favorable rulings in the majority of criminal cases."<sup id="cite_ref-countryreport_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countryreport-113">[107]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>Kazakhstan's global rank in the <a href="/wiki/World_Justice_Project" title="World Justice Project">World Justice Project</a>'s 2015 Rule of Law Index was 65 out of 102; the country scored well on "Order and Security" (global rank 32/102), and poorly on "Constraints on Government Powers" (global rank 93/102), "Open Government" (85/102) and "Fundamental Rights" (84/102, with a downward trend marking a deterioration in conditions).<sup id="cite_ref-WJP2015_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WJP2015-114">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/ABA_Rule_of_Law_Initiative" title="ABA Rule of Law Initiative">ABA Rule of Law Initiative</a> of the American Bar Association has programs to train justice sector professionals in Kazakhstan.<sup id="cite_ref-ABArol_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABArol-115">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ABAback_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABAback-116">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan's Supreme Court has taken recent steps to modernise and to increase transparency and oversight over the country's legal system. With funding from the US Agency for International Development, the ABA Rule of Law Initiative began a new program in April 2012 to strengthen the independence and accountability of Kazakhstan's judiciary.<sup id="cite_ref-ABAjr_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABAjr-117">[111]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In an effort to increase transparency in the criminal justice and court system, and improve human rights, Kazakhstan intends to digitise all investigative, prosecutorial and court records by 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-digitise_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-digitise-118">[112]</a></sup> Many criminal cases are closed before trial on the basis of reconciliation between the defendant and the victim because they simplify the work of the law-enforcement officers, release the defendant from punishment, and pay little regard to the victim's rights.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Homosexuality has been legal in Kazakhstan since 1997; though it is still socially unacceptable in most areas.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[114]</a></sup> Discrimination against <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Kazakhstan" title="LGBT rights in Kazakhstan">LGBT people</a> in Kazakhstan is widespread.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[116]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Kazakhstan" title="Economy of Kazakhstan">Economy of Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Central_Downtown_Astana_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Central_Downtown_Astana_2.jpg/300px-Central_Downtown_Astana_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Central_Downtown_Astana_2.jpg/450px-Central_Downtown_Astana_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Central_Downtown_Astana_2.jpg/600px-Central_Downtown_Astana_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Central_Downtown_Astana_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Downtown of <a href="/wiki/Nur-Sultan" title="Nur-Sultan">Nur-Sultan</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kazakhstan has the largest and strongest performing economy in Central Asia. Supported by rising oil output and prices, Kazakhstan's economy grew at an average of 8% per year until 2013, before suffering a slowdown in 2014 and 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-imfarticleiv_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfarticleiv-123">[117]</a></sup> Kazakhstan was the first former Soviet Republic to repay all of its debt to the International Monetary Fund, 7 years ahead of schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-IMFrepay_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMFrepay-124">[118]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan has a GDP of $179.332&nbsp;billion and an annual growth rate of 4.5%. Per capita, Kazakhstan's GDP stands at $9,686.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[119]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> Kazakhstan ranks third, after China and Qatar, among the 25 most dynamic economies of the 21st century's first decade. Kazakhstan's increased role in global trade and central positioning on the new Silk Road has given the country the potential to open its markets to billions of people. Kazakhstan joined the World Trade Organisation in 2015. </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Astana,_capital_of_Kazakhstan_08.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Astana%2C_capital_of_Kazakhstan_08.jpg/220px-Astana%2C_capital_of_Kazakhstan_08.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Astana%2C_capital_of_Kazakhstan_08.jpg/330px-Astana%2C_capital_of_Kazakhstan_08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Astana%2C_capital_of_Kazakhstan_08.jpg/440px-Astana%2C_capital_of_Kazakhstan_08.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1199"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Astana,_capital_of_Kazakhstan_08.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Khan_Shatyr_Entertainment_Center" title="Khan Shatyr Entertainment Center">Khan Shatyr Entertainment Center</a> in Nur-Sultan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Buoyed by high world <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a> prices, GDP growth figures were between 8.9% and 13.5% from 2000 to 2007 before decreasing to 1–3% in 2008 and 2009, and then rising again from 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[120]</a></sup> Other major exports of Kazakhstan include wheat, textiles, and livestock. Kazakhstan is a leading exporter of uranium.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan's economy grew by 4.6% in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-BRICplus_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BRICplus-129">[123]</a></sup> The country experienced a slowdown in economic growth from 2014 sparked by falling oil prices and the effects of the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_crisis" title="Ukrainian crisis">Ukrainian crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[124]</a></sup> The country devalued its currency by 19% in February 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[125]</a></sup> Another 22% devaluation occurred in August 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[126]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan's fiscal situation is stable. The government has continued to follow a conservative fiscal policy by controlling budget spending and accumulating oil revenue savings in its Oil Fund – Samruk-Kazyna. The global financial crisis forced Kazakhstan to increase its public borrowing to support the economy. Public debt increased to 13.4 per cent in 2013 from 8.7 per cent in 2008. Between 2012 and 2013, the government achieved an overall fiscal surplus of 4.5 per cent.<sup id="cite_ref-kzwbprofile_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kzwbprofile-133">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 2002, Kazakhstan has sought to manage strong inflows of foreign currency without sparking inflation. Inflation has not been under strict control, however, registering 6.6% in 2002, 6.8% in 2003, and 6.4% in 2004. </p>
      <p>In March 2002, the <a href="/wiki/US_Department_of_Commerce" class="mw-redirect" title="US Department of Commerce">US Department of Commerce</a> granted Kazakhstan <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a> status under <a href="/wiki/Trade_Act_of_2002" title="Trade Act of 2002">US trade law</a>. This change in status recognised substantive market economy reforms in the areas of currency convertibility, wage rate determination, openness to foreign investment, and government control over the means of production and allocation of resources. </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan weathered the global financial crisis well,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> by combining fiscal relaxation with monetary stabilisation. In 2009, the government introduced large-scale support measures such as the recapitalisation of banks and support for the real estate and agricultural sectors, as well as for small and medium enterprises (SMEs). The total value of the stimulus programs amounted to $21&nbsp;billion, or 20 per cent of the country's GDP, with $4&nbsp;billion going to stabilise the financial sector.<sup id="cite_ref-ft21bn_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ft21bn-134">[128]</a></sup> During the global economic crisis, Kazakhstan's economy contracted by 1.2% in 2009, while the annual growth rate subsequently increased to 7.5% and 5% in 2011 and 2012, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-imfarticleiv_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfarticleiv-123">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:35Aktau_g%C5%82%C3%B3wna_ulica.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/35Aktau_g%C5%82%C3%B3wna_ulica.JPG/220px-35Aktau_g%C5%82%C3%B3wna_ulica.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/35Aktau_g%C5%82%C3%B3wna_ulica.JPG/330px-35Aktau_g%C5%82%C3%B3wna_ulica.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/35Aktau_g%C5%82%C3%B3wna_ulica.JPG/440px-35Aktau_g%C5%82%C3%B3wna_ulica.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:35Aktau_g%C5%82%C3%B3wna_ulica.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Aktau" title="Aktau">Aktau</a> is Kazakhstan's only seaport on the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In September 2002, Kazakhstan became the first country in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a> to receive an investment grade <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating" title="Credit rating">credit rating</a> from a major international <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating_agency" title="Credit rating agency">credit rating agency</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> As of late December 2003, Kazakhstan's gross foreign debt was about $22.9&nbsp;billion. Total governmental debt was $4.2&nbsp;billion, 14% of GDP. There has been a reduction in the ratio of debt to GDP. The ratio of total governmental debt to GDP in 2000, was 21.7%; in 2001, it was 17.5%, and in 2002, it was 15.4%. It has risen to 19.2% in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[129]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Economic growth, combined with earlier <a href="/wiki/Tax_reform" title="Tax reform">tax</a> and financial sector reforms, has dramatically improved government finance from the 1999 <a href="/wiki/Budget_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Budget deficit">budget deficit</a> level of 3.5% of GDP to a deficit of 1.2% of GDP in 2003. Government revenues grew from 19.8% of GDP in 1999 to 22.6% of GDP in 2001, but decreased to 16.2% of GDP in 2003. In 2000, Kazakhstan adopted a new <a href="/wiki/Tax_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Tax code">tax code</a> in an effort to consolidate these gains. </p>
      <p>On 29 November 2003, the Law on Changes to Tax Code which reduced <a href="/wiki/Tax_rates_around_the_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Tax rates around the world">tax rates</a> was adopted. The <a href="/wiki/Value_added_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Value added tax">value added tax</a> fell from 16% to 15%, the social tax, payable by all employers, from 21% to 20%, and the personal <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a>, from 30% to 20%. On 7 July 2006, the personal income tax was reduced even further to a flat rate of 5% for personal income in the form of dividends and 10% for other personal income. Kazakhstan furthered its reforms by adopting a new land code on 20 June 2003, and a new customs code on 5 April 2003. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2013Kazakhstani_imports.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/2013Kazakhstani_imports.PNG/350px-2013Kazakhstani_imports.PNG" decoding="async" width="350" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/2013Kazakhstani_imports.PNG/525px-2013Kazakhstani_imports.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/2013Kazakhstani_imports.PNG/700px-2013Kazakhstani_imports.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1680" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2013Kazakhstani_imports.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Kazakhstan's imports, 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kazakhstan_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Kazakhstan_Export_Treemap.jpg/350px-Kazakhstan_Export_Treemap.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Kazakhstan_Export_Treemap.jpg/525px-Kazakhstan_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Kazakhstan_Export_Treemap.jpg/700px-Kazakhstan_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2668" data-file-height="2085"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kazakhstan_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of Kazakhstan's exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kashagan_Oil_Field,_Kazakhstan_by_Planet_Labs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Kashagan_Oil_Field%2C_Kazakhstan_by_Planet_Labs.jpg/220px-Kashagan_Oil_Field%2C_Kazakhstan_by_Planet_Labs.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Kashagan_Oil_Field%2C_Kazakhstan_by_Planet_Labs.jpg/330px-Kashagan_Oil_Field%2C_Kazakhstan_by_Planet_Labs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Kashagan_Oil_Field%2C_Kazakhstan_by_Planet_Labs.jpg/440px-Kashagan_Oil_Field%2C_Kazakhstan_by_Planet_Labs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3772" data-file-height="2830"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kashagan_Oil_Field,_Kazakhstan_by_Planet_Labs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Aerial view of <a href="/wiki/Kashagan_Field" title="Kashagan Field">Kashagan Oil Field</a> structures
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Energy is the leading economic sector. Production of crude oil and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_condensate" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural gas condensate">natural gas condensate</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Oil_and_gas_basins_of_Kazakhstan" title="Oil and gas basins of Kazakhstan">oil and gas basins of Kazakhstan</a> amounted to 79.2&nbsp;million tonnes (77.9&nbsp;million <a href="/wiki/Long_ton" title="Long ton">long tons</a>; 87.3&nbsp;million <a href="/wiki/Short_ton" title="Short ton">short tons</a>) in 2012 up from 51.2&nbsp;million tonnes (50.4&nbsp;million long tons; 56.4&nbsp;million short tons) in 2003. Kazakhstan raised oil and gas condensate exports to 44.3&nbsp;million tons in 2003, 13% higher than in 2002. Gas production in Kazakhstan in 2003, amounted to 13.9&nbsp;billion cubic metres (490&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/1000000000_(number)" class="mw-redirect" title="1000000000 (number)">billion</a> <a href="/wiki/Cubic_foot" title="Cubic foot">cubic feet</a>), up 22.7% compared to 2002, including natural gas production of 7.3&nbsp;billion cubic metres (260&nbsp;billion cubic feet). Kazakhstan holds about 4&nbsp;billion tonnes (3.9&nbsp;billion long tons; 4.4&nbsp;billion short tons) of proven recoverable oil reserves and 2,000 cubic kilometres (480 cubic miles) of gas. Kazakhstan is the 19th largest oil-producing nation in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[130]</a></sup> Kazakhstan's oil exports in 2003, were valued at more than $7&nbsp;billion, representing 65% of overall exports and 24% of the GDP. Major oil and gas fields and recoverable <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">oil reserves</a> are <a href="/wiki/Tengiz_Field" title="Tengiz Field">Tengiz</a> with 7 billion barrels (1.1&nbsp;billion cubic metres); <a href="/wiki/Karachaganak_Field" title="Karachaganak Field">Karachaganak</a> with 8 billion barrels (1.3&nbsp;billion cubic metres) and 1,350 cubic kilometres (320 cubic miles) of natural gas; and <a href="/wiki/Kashagan_Field" title="Kashagan Field">Kashagan</a> with 7 to 9 billion barrels (1.4&nbsp;billion cubic metres). </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan instituted an ambitious pension reform program in 1998. As of 1 January 2012, the pension assets were about $17&nbsp;billion (KZT 2.5&nbsp;trillion). There are 11 saving pension funds in the country. The State Accumulating Pension Fund, the only state-owned fund, was <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatised</a> in 2006. The country's unified financial regulatory agency oversees and regulates the pension funds. The growing demand of the pension funds for quality investment outlets triggered rapid development of the debt <a href="/wiki/Security_(finance)" title="Security (finance)">securities</a> market. Pension fund capital is being invested almost exclusively in corporate and government <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a>, including government of Kazakhstan Eurobonds. The government of Kazakhstan is studying a project to create a unified national pension fund and transfer all the accounts from the private pension funds into it.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The banking system of Kazakhstan is developing rapidly and the system's capitalisation now<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> exceeds $1&nbsp;billion. The <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Kazakhstan" title="National Bank of Kazakhstan">National Bank</a> has introduced deposit insurance in its campaign to strengthen the banking sector. Due to troubling and non-performing bad assets the bank sector yet is at risk to lose stability. Several major foreign banks have branches in Kazakhstan, including <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Scotland" title="Royal Bank of Scotland">RBS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citibank" title="Citibank">Citibank</a>, and <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kookmin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kookmin (page does not exist)">Kookmin</a> and <a href="/wiki/UniCredit" title="UniCredit">UniCredit</a> have both recently entered the Kazakhstan's financial services market through acquisitions and <a href="/wiki/Equity_(finance)" title="Equity (finance)">stake</a>-building. </p>
      <p>According to the 2010–11 World Economic Forum in Global Competitiveness Report, Kazakhstan was ranked 72nd in the world in economic competitiveness.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[132]</a></sup> One year later, the <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">Global Competitiveness Report</a> ranked Kazakhstan 50th in most competitive markets.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2012, Kazakhstan attracted $14&nbsp;billion of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> inflows into the country at a 7% growth rate making it the most attractive place to invest out of <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a> nations.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[134]</a></sup> In 2018, $24&nbsp;billion of FDI was directed into Kazakhstan, a significant increase since 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[135]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/Aftenposten" title="Aftenposten">Aftenposten</a></i> quoted the human-rights activist and lawyer <a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Jivaga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Denis Jivaga (page does not exist)">Denis Jivaga</a> as saying that there is an "<a href="/wiki/Oil_fund" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil fund">oil fund</a> in Kazakhstan, but nobody knows how the income is spent".<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan climbed to 41st on the 2018 Economic Freedom Index published by the Wall Street Journal and The Heritage Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-EFI2018_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EFI2018-143">[137]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan's economy grew at an average of 8% per year over the past decade on the back of hydrocarbon exports.<sup id="cite_ref-imfarticleiv_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfarticleiv-123">[117]</a></sup> Despite the lingering uncertainty of the global economy, Kazakhstan's economy has been stable. GDP growth in January–September 2013 was 5.7%, according to preliminary calculations of the Ministry Economy and Budget Planning.<sup id="cite_ref-kzgdp2013_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kzgdp2013-144">[138]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From January to September 2014 Kazakhstan's GDP grew at 4%.<sup id="cite_ref-BSt1_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BSt1-145">[139]</a></sup> According to the results from the first half of the year, the current account surplus is $6.6&nbsp;billion, a figure two times higher than that of the first half of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-BSt1_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BSt1-145">[139]</a></sup> According to the Chairman of the National Bank of Kazakhstan, Kairat Kelimbetov, the increase was caused by a trade surplus of 17.4 percent, or approximately US$22.6&nbsp;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-BSt1_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BSt1-145">[139]</a></sup> The overall inflation rate for 2014 is forecasted at 7.4 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-BSt1_145-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BSt1-145">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>China is one of the main economic and trade partners of Kazakhstan. In 2013, China launched the Belt and Road Initiative (BRI) where Kazakhstan is given an important role as a transit hub.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[140]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_trade">Foreign trade</span></h3> 
      <p>Kazakhstan's foreign trade turnover in 2018 was $93.5 billion, which is 19.7% more compared to 2017. Export in 2018 reached $67 billion (+25.7% vs 2017) and import was $32.5 billion (+9.9% vs 2017).<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[141]</a></sup> Exports accounted for 40.1% of Kazakhstan's gross domestic product (GDP) in 2018. Kazakhstan exports 800 products to 120 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[142]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Kazakhstan" title="Agriculture in Kazakhstan">Agriculture in Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B6%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B0(3264-2448).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B6%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B0%283264-2448%29.jpg/220px-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B6%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B0%283264-2448%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B6%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B0%283264-2448%29.jpg/330px-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B6%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B0%283264-2448%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B6%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B0%283264-2448%29.jpg/440px-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B6%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B0%283264-2448%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BD%D1%8F_%D0%B6%D0%B0%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B0(3264-2448).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Grain fields near <a href="/wiki/Kokshetau" title="Kokshetau">Kokshetau</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Kazakhstan" title="Agriculture in Kazakhstan">Agriculture</a> accounts for approximately 5% of Kazakhstan's GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-8">[4]</a></sup> Grain, potatoes, grapes, vegetables, melons and livestock are the most important agricultural commodities. Agricultural land occupies more than 846,000 square kilometres (327,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). The available agricultural land consists of 205,000 square kilometres (79,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of arable land and 611,000 square kilometres (236,000&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of <a href="/wiki/Pasture" title="Pasture">pasture</a> and hay land. Over 80% of the country's total area is classified as agricultural land, including almost 70% occupied by pasture. Its arable land has the second highest availability per inhabitant (1.5 hectares).<sup id="cite_ref-wb1_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb1-149">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Chief livestock products are <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy products</a>, leather, meat, and <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>. The country's major crops include wheat, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, cotton, and rice. Wheat exports, a major source of <a href="/wiki/Hard_currency" title="Hard currency">hard currency</a>, rank among the leading commodities in Kazakhstan's export trade. In 2003 Kazakhstan harvested 17.6&nbsp;million tons of grain in gross, 2.8% higher compared to 2002. Kazakhstani agriculture still has many environmental problems from mismanagement during its years in the Soviet Union. Some <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_wine" title="Kazakh wine">Kazakh wine</a> is produced in the mountains to the east of Almaty.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan is thought to be one of the places that the apple originated, particularly the wild <a href="/wiki/Ancestor" title="Ancestor">ancestor</a> of <i>Malus domestica</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Malus_sieversii" title="Malus sieversii">Malus sieversii</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[145]</a></sup> It has no common name in English, but is known in its native Kazakhstan as <i>alma</i>. The region where it is thought to originate is called <i>Almaty</i>: "rich with apple".<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[146]</a></sup> This tree is still found wild in the mountains of Central Asia, in southern Kazakhstan, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> in China. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Kazakhstan" title="Transport in Kazakhstan">Transport in Kazakhstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Kazakhstan" title="Telecommunications in Kazakhstan">Telecommunications in Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Railways provide 68% of all cargo and passenger traffic to over 57% of the country. There are 15,333&nbsp;km (9,527&nbsp;mi) in common carrier service, excluding industrial lines.<sup id="cite_ref-ciafactbook_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciafactbook-153">[147]</a></sup>15,333&nbsp;km (9,527&nbsp;mi) of <a href="/wiki/5_ft_and_1520_mm_gauge_railways" title="5 ft and 1520 mm gauge railways"><span class="nowrap">1,520&nbsp;mm</span></a> (<span class="nowrap">4&nbsp;ft&nbsp;<span class="frac">11<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r993651011">.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px;white-space:nowrap}</style><span class="sr-only">&nbsp;</span><sup>27</sup>⁄<sub>32</sub></span>&nbsp;in</span>) gauge, 4,000&nbsp;km (2,500&nbsp;mi) electrified, in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-ciafactbook_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciafactbook-153">[147]</a></sup> Most cities are connected by railroad; high-speed trains go from <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a> (the southernmost city) to <a href="/wiki/Petropavl" title="Petropavl">Petropavl</a> (the northernmost city) in about 18 hours. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Railway_Map_of_Kazakhstan_(kk).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Railway_Map_of_Kazakhstan_%28kk%29.png/220px-Railway_Map_of_Kazakhstan_%28kk%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Railway_Map_of_Kazakhstan_%28kk%29.png/330px-Railway_Map_of_Kazakhstan_%28kk%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Railway_Map_of_Kazakhstan_%28kk%29.png/440px-Railway_Map_of_Kazakhstan_%28kk%29.png 2x" data-file-width="4134" data-file-height="2362"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Railway_Map_of_Kazakhstan_(kk).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Kazakhstan railway network
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:KTZ_2TE10U_Aynabulak.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/KTZ_2TE10U_Aynabulak.jpg/220px-KTZ_2TE10U_Aynabulak.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/KTZ_2TE10U_Aynabulak.jpg/330px-KTZ_2TE10U_Aynabulak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/KTZ_2TE10U_Aynabulak.jpg/440px-KTZ_2TE10U_Aynabulak.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4364" data-file-height="2694"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:KTZ_2TE10U_Aynabulak.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Train 22 Kyzylorda – Semipalatinsk, hauled by a Kazakhstan Temir Zholy 2TE10U diesel locomotive. Picture taken near Aynabulak, Kazakhstan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan_Temir_Zholy" title="Kazakhstan Temir Zholy">Kazakhstan Temir Zholy</a> (KTZ) is the national railway company. KTZ cooperates with French loco manufacturer Alstom in developing Kazakhstan's railway infrastructure. Alstom has more than 600 staff and two joint ventures with KTZ and its subsidiary in Kazakhstan.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[148]</a></sup> In July 2017, Alstom opened its first locomotive repairing center in Kazakhstan. It is the only repairing center in Central Asia and the Caucasus.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As the Kazakhstani rail system was designed during the Soviet era, rail routes were designed ignoring intersoviet borders and to the needs of Soviet planning. This has caused anomalies such as the route from <a href="/wiki/Oral,_Kazakhstan" title="Oral, Kazakhstan">Oral</a> to <a href="/wiki/Aktobe" title="Aktobe">Aktobe</a> now passes briefly through Russian territory.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Astana_Nurly_Zhol_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Astana Nurly Zhol railway station">Astana Nurly Zhol railway station</a>, the most modern railway station in Kazakhstan, was opened in Nur-Sultan on 31 May 2017. The opening of the station coincided with the start of the <a href="/wiki/Expo_2017" title="Expo 2017">Expo 2017</a> international exhibition. According to Kazakhstan Railways (KTZ), the 120,000m2 station is expected to be used by 54 trains a day and has capacity to handle 35,000 passengers a day.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[150]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The strategy of transport development in Kazakhstan until 2015 is to build 1,600&nbsp;km (990&nbsp;mi) of new electrified and 2,700&nbsp;km (1,700&nbsp;mi) of existing railway stations. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE_014.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE_014.JPG/170px-%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE_014.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE_014.JPG/255px-%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE_014.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE_014.JPG/340px-%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%BC%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B5_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%80%D0%BE_014.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="2400"></a>

      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%83.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Almaty Metro
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There is a small 8.56&nbsp;km (5.32&nbsp;mi) <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro</a> system in <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>. A second and third metro lines are planned in the future. The second line would intersect with the first line at <a href="/wiki/Alatau_(Almaty_Metro)" title="Alatau (Almaty Metro)">Alatau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zhibek_Zholy_(Almaty_Metro)" title="Zhibek Zholy (Almaty Metro)">Zhibek Zholy</a> stations.<sup id="cite_ref-urbanrail.net_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urbanrail.net-157">[151]</a></sup> In May 2011, the construction of the second phase of the Almaty Metro line 1 began. The general contractor is Almatymetrokurylys. Currently more than 300&nbsp;m (980&nbsp;ft) of tunnels on the extension project have been excavated. The extension includes five new stations, and will connect the downtown area of Almaty with <a href="/wiki/Kalkaman" title="Kalkaman">Kalkaman</a> in the suburbs. Its length will be 8.62&nbsp;km (5.36&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-Almaty_metro_website_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Almaty_metro_website-158">[152]</a></sup> The construction is divided into 3 phases. The first phase (the current phase) will be the addition of two stations: Sairan and Moscow, a length of 2.7&nbsp;km (1.7&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-Almaty_metro_website_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Almaty_metro_website-158">[152]</a></sup> For more details see: <a href="/wiki/Almaty_Metro" title="Almaty Metro">Almaty Metro</a>.There was a tram system of 10 lines which operated from 1937 to 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[153]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Astana_Metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Astana Metro">Astana Metro</a> system is under construction. It's been a long time coming and the project was abandoned at one point in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[154]</a></sup> but an agreement was signed on 7 May 2015 for the project to go ahead.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[155]</a></sup> The system was opened between 1959 and 1978, and the tram was a popular form of transport in Oskemen/Ust-Kamenogorsk until its closure in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[156]</a></sup> At its peak it had six routes, but in the end it had four routes in operation. It had a fleet of 50 working tram cars.<sup id="cite_ref-Oskemen_Trmway_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oskemen_Trmway-163">[157]</a></sup> There is an 86&nbsp;km (53&nbsp;mi) tram network, which began service in 1965 with, As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kazakhstan&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 20 regular and three special routes. The network has a 60% share of the local public transport market. Its fleet of 115 trams are due to be replaced and in 2012, the city announced plans to purchase 100 new trams.<sup id="cite_ref-Pavlodar_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pavlodar-164">[158]</a></sup> There are two tram lines in this city.<sup id="cite_ref-Temirtau_city_council_website_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Temirtau_city_council_website-165">[159]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Khorgos Gateway dry port is one of Kazakhstan's primary dry ports for handling trans-Eurasian trains, which travel more than 9,000&nbsp;km (5,600&nbsp;mi) between China and Europe. The Khorgos Gateway dry port is surrounded by Khorgos Eastern Gate SEZ that officially commenced operations in December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2009 the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> blacklisted all Kazakh air carriers with a sole exception of <a href="/wiki/Air_Astana" title="Air Astana">Air Astana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[161]</a></sup> Since then, Kazakhstan has consistently taken measures to modernise and revamp its air safety oversight. In 2016 the European air safety authorities removed all Kazakh airlines from the blacklist and there was "sufficient evidence of compliance" with international standards by Kazakh Airlines and the Civil Aviation Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[162]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining_and_Metallurgy">Mining and Metallurgy</span></h3> 
      <p>Kazakhstan has vast deposits of uranium, precious metals, metals, ores, alloys, ferroalloys and minerals.<sup id="cite_ref-mining_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mining-169">[163]</a></sup> </p>
