decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8D%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%A2%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%88%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%28%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_1%29_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B5_2015.jpg/330px-%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8D%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%A2%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%88%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%28%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_1%29_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B5_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8D%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%A2%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%88%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%28%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_1%29_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B5_2015.jpg/440px-%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8D%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%A2%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%88%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_%28%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_1%29_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B5_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="1633"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8D%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%A2%D1%83%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%88%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B0_(%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%8C_1)_%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%94%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BD%D0%B5_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan_in_the_Junior_Eurovision_Song_Contest_2018#Daneliya_Tuleshova" title="Kazakhstan in the Junior Eurovision Song Contest 2018">Daneliya Tuleshova</a> represented Kazakhstan at the <a href="/wiki/Junior_Eurovision_Song_Contest_2018" title="Junior Eurovision Song Contest 2018">Junior Eurovision Song Contest 2018</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Russian influence on the music life in Kazakhstan can be seen in two spheres: first, the introduction of musical academic institutions such as concert houses with opera stages, conservatories, where the European music was performed and taught, and second, by trying to incorporate Kazakh traditional music into these academic structures. Controlled first by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> and then the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, Kazakhstan's folk and classical traditions became connected with <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Russian_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic Russian music">ethnic Russian music</a> and Western European music. Prior to the 20th century, Kazakh folk music was collected and studied by <a href="/wiki/Ethnography" title="Ethnography">ethnographic</a> research teams including composers, music critics and <a href="/wiki/Musicology" title="Musicology">musicologists</a>. In the first part of the 19th century, Kazakh music was transcribed in linear <a href="/wiki/Musical_notation" title="Musical notation">notation</a>. Some composers of this era set Kazakh folk songs to Russian-style <a href="/wiki/European_classical_music" class="mw-redirect" title="European classical music">European classical music</a>. </p>
      <p>The Kazakhs themselves, however, did not write their own music in notation until 1931. Later, as part of the Soviet Union, Kazakh folk culture was encouraged in a sanitised manner designed to avoid political and social unrest. The result was a bland derivative of real Kazakh folk music. In 1920, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Zatayevich" title="Aleksandr Zatayevich">Aleksandr Zatayevich</a>, a Russian official, created major works of art music with melodies and other elements of Kazakh folk music. Beginning in 1928 and accelerating in the 1930s, he also adapted traditional Kazakh instruments for use in Russian-style ensembles, such as by increasing the number of <a href="/wiki/Fret" title="Fret">frets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Strings_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Strings (music)">strings</a>. Soon, these styles of modern orchestral playing became the only way for musicians to officially play; Kazakh folk was turned into patriotic, professional and socialist endeavours <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://src-h.slav.hokudai.ac.jp/publictn/46/touda/touda-eng.html">From Folklore to Soviet National Culture- The Process of Formation of "Kazak National Music"(1920-1942)-</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Astudio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Astudio.jpg/220px-Astudio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Astudio.jpg/330px-Astudio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Astudio.jpg/440px-Astudio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Astudio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/A-Studio" title="A-Studio">A-Studio</a> was created in 1982 in <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a>, then called Alma-Ata, hence called "Alma-Ata Studio"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The current situation could be described as the effort to rediscover the traditional music as it had been practised before the heavy influence of European musical styles. Although the quality of the performances and the striving for authenticity cannot be ignored, it is for methodological reasons important to remember that the contemporary musicians performing among traditional folk music are all well trained professionals (Rauchan Orazbaeva, Ramazan Stamgazi). </p>
      <p>Another very challenging aspect arises from the young composers generation, and the rock and jazz musicians, as they aim to incorporate their traditional heritage into the music they learned from the western cultures, thus forming a new stage of "ethnic contemporary classics", respectively ethnic rock or jazz music that sounds distinctly Kazakh. For the classical sector outstanding: Aqtoty Raimkulova, <a href="/wiki/Turan_ensemble" title="Turan ensemble">Turan ensemble</a>; for jazz: "Magic of Nomads"; for rock: Roksonaki, <a href="/wiki/Urker" title="Urker">Urker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulytau" title="Ulytau">Ulytau</a>, Alda span. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_arts">Fine arts</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_art" title="Kazakh art">Kazakh art</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In Kazakhstan, the fine arts in the classical sense has its origins in the second half of the 19th century - the beginning of the 20th century. It was largely influenced by Russian artists, such as Vasily Vereshchagin and Nikolai Khludov, who internsively travelled in Central Asia. Khludov had a particular influence on the development of the local school of painting, becoming the teacher of many local artists. The most famous of these is Abilkhan Kasteyev, after whom the State Museum of Art of Kazakhstan was renamed in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[249]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Kazakh school of fine arts was fully formed by the 1940s, and flourished in the 1950s. Local painters, graphic artists and sculptors, trained under the unified Soviet system of artist education, began active work, often using national motifs in their art. The painters O. Tansykbaev, J. Shardenov, K. Telzhanov, and S. Aitbaev, graphic artists E. Sidorkina and A. Duzelkhanov, and sculptors H. Nauryzbaeva and E. Sergebaeva are today counted among the key figures of Kazakhstani art. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_cuisine" title="Kazakh cuisine">Kazakh cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the national cuisine, livestock meat can be cooked in a variety of ways and is usually served with a wide assortment of traditional bread products. Refreshments include black tea, often served with milk and dry fruits (such as dry apricots) and nuts. In southern provinces, people often prefer green tea. Traditional milk-derived drinks such as <a href="/wiki/Ayran" title="Ayran">ayran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shubat" class="mw-redirect" title="Shubat">shubat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kymyz" class="mw-redirect" title="Kymyz">kymyz</a>. A traditional Kazakh dinner involves a multitude of appetisers on the table, followed by a soup and one or two main courses such as <a href="/wiki/Pilaf" title="Pilaf">pilaf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beshbarmak" title="Beshbarmak">beshbarmak</a>. They also drink their national beverage, which consists of fermented mare's milk.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[250]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Kazakhstan" title="Sport in Kazakhstan">Sport in Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2016_Brussels_Cycling_Classic_032.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/2016_Brussels_Cycling_Classic_032.jpg/220px-2016_Brussels_Cycling_Classic_032.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/2016_Brussels_Cycling_Classic_032.jpg/330px-2016_Brussels_Cycling_Classic_032.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/2016_Brussels_Cycling_Classic_032.jpg/440px-2016_Brussels_Cycling_Classic_032.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1968" data-file-height="1477"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2016_Brussels_Cycling_Classic_032.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Astana_Pro_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="Astana Pro Team">Astana Pro Team</a> is professional cycling team representing Kazakhstan and sponsored by the state-owned companies from Kazakhstan
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kazakhstan consistently performs in Olympic competitions. It is especially successful in <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>. This has brought some attention to the Central Asian nation and increased world awareness of its athletes. <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Karpov" class="mw-redirect" title="Dmitry Karpov">Dmitry Karpov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Olga_Rypakova" title="Olga Rypakova">Olga Rypakova</a> are among the most notable Kazakhstani athletics. <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Karpov" class="mw-redirect" title="Dmitry Karpov">Dmitry Karpov</a> is a distinguished decathlete, taking bronze in both the <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2003_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2003 World Championships in Athletics">2003</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Athletics_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 World Athletics Championships">2007 World Athletics Championships</a>. <a href="/wiki/Olga_Rypakova" title="Olga Rypakova">Olga Rypakova</a> is an athlete, specialised in <a href="/wiki/Triple_jump" title="Triple jump">triple jump</a> (women's), taking silver in the <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2011 World Championships in Athletics">2011 World Championships in Athletics</a> and Gold in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>. </p>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:FC_Astana_vs._Celtic_FC_UCL_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/FC_Astana_vs._Celtic_FC_UCL_2017.jpg/220px-FC_Astana_vs._Celtic_FC_UCL_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/FC_Astana_vs._Celtic_FC_UCL_2017.jpg/330px-FC_Astana_vs._Celtic_FC_UCL_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/FC_Astana_vs._Celtic_FC_UCL_2017.jpg/440px-FC_Astana_vs._Celtic_FC_UCL_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3024" data-file-height="1840"></a>

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kazakhstan's city of <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a> submitted twice bid for the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter Olympics">Winter Olympics</a>: in <a href="/wiki/Almaty_bid_for_the_2014_Winter_Olympics" title="Almaty bid for the 2014 Winter Olympics">2014</a> and again for the <a href="/wiki/2022_Winter_Olympics" title="2022 Winter Olympics">2022 Winter Olympics</a>. <a href="/wiki/Nur-Sultan" title="Nur-Sultan">Nur-Sultan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Almaty" title="Almaty">Almaty</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/2011_Asian_Winter_Games" title="2011 Asian Winter Games">2011 Asian Winter Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[251]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Popular sports in Kazakhstan include football, basketball, ice hockey, bandy, and boxing. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dusan_Petronijevic.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Dusan_Petronijevic.jpg/220px-Dusan_Petronijevic.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Dusan_Petronijevic.jpg/330px-Dusan_Petronijevic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Dusan_Petronijevic.jpg/440px-Dusan_Petronijevic.jpg 2x" data-file-width="664" data-file-height="362"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dusan_Petronijevic.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/FC_Shakhter_Karagandy" title="FC Shakhter Karagandy">FC Shakhter Karagandy</a> players
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Kazakhstan. The <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_Kazakhstan" title="Football Federation of Kazakhstan">Football Federation of Kazakhstan</a> is the sport's national governing body. The FFK organises the <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan_national_football_team" title="Kazakhstan national football team">men's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Kazakhstan women's national football team">women's</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a> national teams. </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan's most famous basketball player was <a href="/wiki/Alzhan_Zharmukhamedov" title="Alzhan Zharmukhamedov">Alzhan Zharmukhamedov</a>, who played for <a href="/wiki/PBC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PBC CSKA Moscow">CSKA Moscow</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union%27s_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet Union's national basketball team">Soviet Union's national basketball team</a> in the 1960s and 1970s. Throughout his career, he won multiple titles and medals at some of the world's most prestigious basketball competitions, including the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Basketball at the Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Basketball World Cup">Basketball World Cup</a>, the <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket" title="EuroBasket">EuroBasket</a> (the European Basketball Championship), and the <a href="/wiki/EuroLeague" title="EuroLeague">EuroLeague</a>. In 1971 he earned the title <a href="/wiki/Unified_Sports_Classification_System_of_the_USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Unified Sports Classification System of the USSR">Master of Sports of the USSR, International Class</a> and a year later he was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Badge_of_Honor" class="mw-redirect" title="Order of the Badge of Honor">Order of the Badge of Honor</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan%27s_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazakhstan's national basketball team">Kazakhstan's national basketball team</a> was established in 1992, after the dissolution of the Soviet Union. Since its foundation, it has been competitive at the continental level. Its greatest accomplishment was at the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_2002_Asian_Games_%E2%80%93_Men" title="Basketball at the 2002 Asian Games – Men">2002 Asian Games</a>, where it defeated the <a href="/wiki/Philippines_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Philippines men's national basketball team">Philippines</a> in its last game to win the bronze medal. At the official <a href="/wiki/Asian_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian Basketball Championship">Asian Basketball Championship</a>, now called <i>FIBA Asia Cup</i>, the Kazakhs' best finish was 4th place in 2007. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Barys_Arena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Barys_Arena.jpg/220px-Barys_Arena.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Barys_Arena.jpg/330px-Barys_Arena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Barys_Arena.jpg/440px-Barys_Arena.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5248" data-file-height="3936"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Barys_Arena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Barys_Arena" title="Barys Arena">Barys Arena</a> in 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan_national_bandy_team" title="Kazakhstan national bandy team">Kazakhstan national bandy team</a> is among the best in the world, and has many times won the bronze medal at the <a href="/wiki/Bandy_World_Championship" title="Bandy World Championship">Bandy World Championship</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/2012_Bandy_World_Championship" title="2012 Bandy World Championship">2012 edition</a> when Kazakhstan hosted the tournament on home ice.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[252]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[253]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2011_Bandy_World_Championship" title="2011 Bandy World Championship">2011 tournament</a>, they were an extra-time in the semi-final from reaching the final for the first time. In 2012, they were even closer when they took it to a penalty shootout. The team won the first <a href="/wiki/Bandy_at_the_2011_Asian_Winter_Games" title="Bandy at the 2011 Asian Winter Games">bandy tournament at the Asian Winter Games</a>. During the Soviet time, Dynamo Alma-Ata won the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Russian_bandy_champions" title="List of Russian bandy champions">Soviet Union national championships</a> in 1977 and 1990 and the <a href="/wiki/European_Cup_(bandy)" title="European Cup (bandy)">European Cup</a> in 1978. Bandy is developed in 10 of the country's 17 administrative divisions (8 of the 14 regions and 2 of the 3 cities which are situated inside of but are not part of regions).<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[254]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Akzhaiyk" class="mw-redirect" title="Akzhaiyk">Akzhaiyk</a> from <a href="/wiki/Oral,_Kazakhstan" title="Oral, Kazakhstan">Oral</a>, however, is the only professional club. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nik_Antropov_Jets_2012-02-11.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Nik_Antropov_Jets_2012-02-11.JPG/150px-Nik_Antropov_Jets_2012-02-11.JPG" decoding="async" width="150" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Nik_Antropov_Jets_2012-02-11.JPG/225px-Nik_Antropov_Jets_2012-02-11.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Nik_Antropov_Jets_2012-02-11.JPG/300px-Nik_Antropov_Jets_2012-02-11.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1539" data-file-height="1922"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nik_Antropov_Jets_2012-02-11.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Antropov" class="mw-redirect" title="Nikolai Antropov">Nikolai Antropov</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Kazakhstan men's national ice hockey team">Kazakh national ice hockey team</a> have competed in <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> in the 1998 and <a href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics" title="2006 Winter Olympics">2006 Winter Olympics</a>, as well as in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Men%27s_World_Ice_Hockey_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="2006 Men's World Ice Hockey Championships">2006 Men's World Ice Hockey Championships</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan_Hockey_Championship" title="Kazakhstan Hockey Championship">Kazakhstan Hockey Championship</a> is held since 1992. <a href="/wiki/Barys_Astana" class="mw-redirect" title="Barys Astana">Barys Astana</a> is the main domestic Kazakhstani ice hockey professional team, and having played in the Kazakhstani national league until the 2008–09 season, when they were transferred to play in the <a href="/wiki/Kontinental_Hockey_League" title="Kontinental Hockey League">Kontinental Hockey League</a>. Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/Kazzinc-Torpedo" title="Kazzinc-Torpedo">Kazzinc-Torpedo</a> and play in the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Hockey_League" title="Supreme Hockey League">Supreme Hockey League</a> since 1996 and the <a href="/wiki/Saryarka_Karagandy" title="Saryarka Karagandy">Saryarka Karagandy</a> since 2012. Top Kazakhstani ice hockey players include <a href="/wiki/Nik_Antropov" title="Nik Antropov">Nik Antropov</a>, Ivan Kulshov and <a href="/wiki/Evgeni_Nabokov" title="Evgeni Nabokov">Evgeni Nabokov</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan_national_amateur_boxing_athletes" title="Kazakhstan national amateur boxing athletes">Kazakh boxers</a> are generally well known in the world. In the last three Olympic Games, their performance was assessed as one of the best and they had more medals than any country in the world, except <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and Russia (in all three games). In 1996 and 2004, three Kazakhstani boxers (<a href="/wiki/Vassiliy_Jirov" title="Vassiliy Jirov">Vassiliy Jirov</a> in 1996, <a href="/wiki/Bakhtiyar_Artayev" title="Bakhtiyar Artayev">Bakhtiyar Artayev</a> in 2004 and <a href="/wiki/Serik_Sapiyev" title="Serik Sapiyev">Serik Sapiyev</a> in 2012) were recognised as the best boxers for their techniques with the <a href="/wiki/Val_Barker_Trophy" title="Val Barker Trophy">Val Barker Trophy</a>, awarded to the best boxer of the tournament. In <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, Kazakhstan performed well in the <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000 Summer Olympics</a> in Sydney. Two boxers, <a href="/wiki/Bekzat_Sattarkhanov" title="Bekzat Sattarkhanov">Bekzat Sattarkhanov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yermakhan_Ibraimov" title="Yermakhan Ibraimov">Yermakhan Ibraimov</a>, earned <a href="/wiki/Gold_medal" title="Gold medal">gold medals</a>. Another two boxers, <a href="/wiki/Bulat_Zhumadilov" title="Bulat Zhumadilov">Bulat Zhumadilov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mukhtarkhan_Dildabekov" title="Mukhtarkhan Dildabekov">Mukhtarkhan Dildabekov</a>, earned <a href="/wiki/Silver_medal" title="Silver medal">silver medals</a>. <a href="/wiki/Oleg_Maskaev" class="mw-redirect" title="Oleg Maskaev">Oleg Maskaev</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Taraz" title="Taraz">Zhambyl</a>, representing Russia, was the <a href="/wiki/World_Boxing_Council" title="World Boxing Council">WBC</a> Heavyweight Champion after knocking out <a href="/wiki/Hasim_Rahman" title="Hasim Rahman">Hasim Rahman</a> on 12 August 2006. The reigning <a href="/wiki/World_Boxing_Association" title="World Boxing Association">WBA</a>, WBC, IBF and <a href="/wiki/International_Boxing_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="International Boxing Organisation">IBO</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_middleweight_boxing_champions" class="mw-redirect" title="List of middleweight boxing champions">middleweight champion</a> is Kazakh boxer <a href="/wiki/Gennady_Golovkin" title="Gennady Golovkin">Gennady Golovkin</a>. <a href="/wiki/Natascha_Ragosina" title="Natascha Ragosina">Natascha Ragosina</a>, representing Russia, but from <a href="/wiki/Karaganda" title="Karaganda">Karaganda</a> held seven versions of the women's super middleweight title, and two heavyweight titles during her boxing career. She holds the record as the longest-reigning WBA female super middleweight champion, and the longest-reigning WBC female super middleweight champion. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Kazakhstan" title="Cinema of Kazakhstan">Cinema of Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%84_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE_II_%D0%91%D0%91_(498).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%84_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE_II_%D0%91%D0%91_%28498%29.JPG/220px-%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%84_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE_II_%D0%91%D0%91_%28498%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%84_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE_II_%D0%91%D0%91_%28498%29.JPG/330px-%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%84_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE_II_%D0%91%D0%91_%28498%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%84_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE_II_%D0%91%D0%91_%28498%29.JPG/440px-%D0%A4%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%84_%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B5%D0%B9_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%BE_II_%D0%91%D0%91_%28498%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Red_Carpet_at_AIAFF.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Red_Carpet_at_AIAFF.jpg/220px-Red_Carpet_at_AIAFF.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Red_Carpet_at_AIAFF.jpg/330px-Red_Carpet_at_AIAFF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Red_Carpet_at_AIAFF.jpg/440px-Red_Carpet_at_AIAFF.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kazakhstan's film industry is run through the state-owned <a href="/wiki/Kazakhfilm" title="Kazakhfilm">Kazakhfilm</a> studios based in Almaty. The studio has produced award-winning movies<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> such as <i><a href="/wiki/Myn_Bala" title="Myn Bala">Myn Bala</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harmony_Lessons" title="Harmony Lessons">Harmony Lessons</a></i>, and <i>Shal</i>. Kazakhstan is host of the <a href="/wiki/International_Astana_Action_Film_Festival" title="International Astana Action Film Festival">International Astana Action Film Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eurasia_International_Film_Festival" title="Eurasia International Film Festival">Eurasia International Film Festival</a> held annually. Hollywood director <a href="/wiki/Timur_Bekmambetov" title="Timur Bekmambetov">Timur Bekmambetov</a> is from Kazakhstan and has become active in bridging Hollywood to the Kazakhstan film industry.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Kazakhstan journalist Artur Platonov won Best Script for his documentary "Sold Souls" about Kazakhstan's contribution to the struggle against terrorism at the 2013 Cannes Corporate Media and TV Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[255]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[256]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Serik Aprymov's <i>Little Brother</i> (<i>Bauyr</i>) won at the Central and Eastern Europe Film Festival <a href="/wiki/GoEast" title="GoEast">goEast</a> from the German Federal Foreign Office.<sup id="cite_ref-EEC_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEC-263">[257]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Kazakhstan" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Kazakhstan">Media of Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Timur_Bekmambetov_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Timur_Bekmambetov_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/150px-Timur_Bekmambetov_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Timur_Bekmambetov_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/225px-Timur_Bekmambetov_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Timur_Bekmambetov_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/300px-Timur_Bekmambetov_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2646" data-file-height="3168"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Timur_Bekmambetov_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Timur_Bekmambetov" title="Timur Bekmambetov">Timur Bekmambetov</a>, a notable Kazakh director
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Kazakhstan is ranked 161 out of 180 countries on the <a href="/wiki/World_Press_Freedom_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="World Press Freedom Index">World Press Freedom Index</a>, compiled by <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[258]</a></sup> A mid-March 2002 <a href="/wiki/Court_order" title="Court order">court order</a>, with the government as a <a href="/wiki/Plaintiff" title="Plaintiff">plaintiff</a>, stated that <i><a href="/wiki/Respublika_(Kazakh_newspaper)" title="Respublika (Kazakh newspaper)">Respublika</a></i> were to stop printing for three months.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-265">[259]</a></sup> The order was evaded by printing under other titles, such as <i>Not That Respublika</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_265-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-265">[259]</a></sup> In early 2014, a court also issued a cease publication order to the small-circulation Assandi-Times newspaper, saying it was a part of the Respublika group. Human Rights Watch said: "this absurd case displays the lengths to which Kazakh authorities are willing to go to bully critical media into silence."<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[260]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With support from the US Department of State's Bureau for Democracy, Human Rights and Labor (DRL), the American Bar Association Rule of Law Initiative opened a media support centre in Almaty to bolster free expression and journalistic rights in Kazakhstan.<sup id="cite_ref-aba_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aba-267">[261]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="UNESCO_World_Heritage_sites">UNESCO World Heritage sites</span></h3> 
      <p>Kazakhstan has three cultural and natural heritages on the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> World Heritage list: the <a href="/wiki/Mausoleum_of_Khoja_Ahmed_Yasawi" title="Mausoleum of Khoja Ahmed Yasawi">Mausoleum of Khoja Ahmed Yassaui</a>, Petroglyphs within the Archaeological Landscape of <a href="/wiki/Tamgaly" title="Tamgaly">Tamgaly</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Korgalzhyn" title="Korgalzhyn">Korgalzhyn</a> and Nauryzumsky reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-UNESCOkz_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCOkz-268">[262]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_holidays">Public holidays</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Kazakhstan" title="Public holidays in Kazakhstan">Public holidays in Kazakhstan</a>
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership_of_international_organisations">Membership of international organisations</span></h2> 
      <p>Kazakhstan's membership of international organisations includes: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> (CIS)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">Shanghai Cooperation Organisation</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Euro-Atlantic_Partnership_Council" title="Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council">Euro-Atlantic Partnership Council</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Individual_Partnership_Action_Plan" title="Individual Partnership Action Plan">Individual Partnership Action Plan</a>, with <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, Ukraine, Georgia, Azerbaijan, Armenia, <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Turkic_Council" title="Turkic Council">Turkic Council</a> and the <a href="/wiki/T%C3%9CRKSOY" class="mw-redirect" title="TÜRKSOY">TÜRKSOY</a> community. (The national language, <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_language" title="Kazakh language">Kazakh</a>, is related to the other <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic languages</a>, with which it shares cultural and <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">historical ties</a>)</li> 
       <li>United Nations</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>, where Kazakhstan is a member of its <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Committee" title="World Heritage Committee">World Heritage Committee</a><sup id="cite_ref-UNESCO_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNESCO-269">[263]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Suppliers_Group" title="Nuclear Suppliers Group">Nuclear Suppliers Group</a> as a participating government</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a><sup id="cite_ref-wtokz_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wtokz-270">[264]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Islamic_Cooperation" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization of Islamic Cooperation">Organization of Islamic Cooperation</a><sup id="cite_ref-oicmems_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oicmems-271">[265]</a></sup></li>
      </ul>

         <li id="cite_note-Beckwith49-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Beckwith49_27-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFBeckwith2009">Beckwith 2009</a>, p.&nbsp;49<span class="error harv-error" style="display: none; font-size:100%"> harvnb error: no target: CITEREFBeckwith2009 (<a href="/wiki/Category:Harv_and_Sfn_template_errors" title="Category:Harv and Sfn template errors">help</a>)</span>: "Archaeologists are now generally agreed that the Andronovo culture of the Central Steppe region in the second millennium BC is to be equated with the Indo-Iranians."</span> </li>

         <li id="cite_note-D_37-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-D_37_29-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFDandamayev1994">Dandamayev 1994</a>, p.&nbsp;37<span class="error harv-error" style="display: none; font-size:100%"> harvnb error: no target: CITEREFDandamayev1994 (<a href="/wiki/Category:Harv_and_Sfn_template_errors" title="Category:Harv and Sfn template errors">help</a>)</span> "In modern scholarship the name 'Sakas' is reserved for the ancient tribes of northern and eastern Central Asia and Eastern Turkestan to distinguish them from the related Massagetae of the Aral region and the Scythians of the Pontic steppes. These tribes spoke Iranian languages, and their chief occupation was nomadic pastoralism."</span> </li>

         <li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFIwiński2006" class="citation web cs1">Iwiński, Tadeusz (7 July 2006). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://assembly.coe.int/nw/xml/XRef/X2H-Xref-ViewHTML.asp?FileID=9998">"Situation in Kazakhstan and its relations with the Council of Europe"</a>. <i>Council of Europe – Parliamentary Assembly</i>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://webcache.googleusercontent.com/search?q=cache:qT4wuwEEvisJ:assembly.coe.int/nw/xml/XRef/X2H-Xref-ViewHTML.asp%3FFileID%3D9998+&amp;cd=1&amp;hl=en&amp;ct=clnk&amp;gl=us&amp;client=firefox-b-1-d">Archived</a> from the original on 15 January 2020<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">14 February</span> 2020</span>. <q>For its part, the Assembly might decide, already at this stage, to interpret Rule 59 of its Rules of procedure, concerning special guests, in such a way as to include Eurasian States. Two Council of Europe member States, Turkey and Russia, belong geographically to both Europe and Asia and are therefore Eurasian. Strictly speaking, the three South Caucasus States, Armenia, Azerbaijan and Georgia are located in Asia, yet their membership of political Europe is no longer in doubt. [...] This being the case, Kazakhstan, as a Eurasian State participating in the OSCE and a signatory to the International covenant on civil and political rights and the International covenant on economic, social and cultural rights, would meet the criteria laid down in Rule 59, making it eligible to apply for special guest status with the Assembly.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Council+of+Europe+%E2%80%93+Parliamentary+Assembly&amp;rft.atitle=Situation+in+Kazakhstan+and+its+relations+with+the+Council+of+Europe&amp;rft.date=2006-07-07&amp;rft.aulast=Iwi%C5%84ski&amp;rft.aufirst=Tadeusz&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fassembly.coe.int%2Fnw%2Fxml%2FXRef%2FX2H-Xref-ViewHTML.asp%3FFileID%3D9998&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AKazakhstan" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>
